Korean Couple, Suspected Drug Dealers, Murdered in Beiping, Leading to Retaliatory Attack

Numerous Koreans Assault Chinese Police Officers That Night

Military Police Impose Temporary Martial Law in the Eastern District

Beiping Correspondence: A murder case involving Koreans occurred here this morning, followed by an incident in the evening where numerous Koreans rioted at a police station and assaulted Chinese police officers. Details of both incidents are as follows:

Zhang Zhuxing, a 38-year-old Korean, and his wife, Ms. Jin, had been living in Beiping for eight years. They rented a house at No. 8 Dalian Keng, using it as a hub for their drug trafficking business. Each room had a pit dug in the ground, allowing heroin customers to secretly hide and consume drugs. Nightly, the traffic in and out never ceased, disturbing the neighborhood and drawing the attention of the police, yet nothing could be done about it. This morning (the 7th) at 7 a.m., Bai Fengshan, a patrol officer from the 12th section of the Third Inner District, was patrolling in front of their door when he suddenly noticed blood flowing from under the doorway. He pushed the door open and saw a corpse lying in the doorway, the face covered in blood. He immediately called the district office, and the director led a team to the scene. They identified the deceased as Zhang Zhuxing, with five axe wounds to the head. Simultaneously, the body of a woman was found in the main room, with multiple axe wounds to the upper body. Two young children were beside the bodies, crying in anguish. In the afternoon, the Public Security Bureau and the court sent personnel to inspect the scene. Bow Ye Liman (transliteration), the head of the Japanese police station (Japanese), also led a team to the scene and even obstructed our court's inspection. Our detective personnel are secretly investigating the truth. Unexpectedly, in the afternoon of the same day, another incident occurred where Koreans assaulted police officers. At around 9 p.m. tonight (the 7th), about fifty or sixty Koreans suddenly arrived at the 12th section police station of the Third Inner District. They stormed into the police station, without saying a word, and indiscriminately smashed everything inside. Telephone and electric light wires were completely cut, and all official documents and records were torn to pieces. Our police officers did not resist and all fled. The head of the patrol officer, An Quanyu (transliteration), was severely injured in the head by the Koreans amidst the chaos and was sent to the hospital for treatment. His life is in danger. Unexpectedly, after the Koreans finished rioting, they marched through the streets in formation, shouting wildly, as if looking for trouble. As a result, the residents of the district closed their doors and warned each other not to go out. For a time, the atmosphere in the eastern district was tense. Our authorities urgently telegraphed various agencies, gathered military police, and detectives, and imposed temporary martial law to inspect idlers and cut off traffic on the streets near the Third Inner District to maintain order. On the one hand, the highest responsible authorities notified the Japanese Embassy's police department, requesting them to send personnel to contact the Koreans to inquire about their intentions so that they could negotiate and cooperate to stop them. As of the time of this report, this riotous spectacle had not been resolved. Whether it is related to the murder case of the Korean in the morning and what the connection is, the truth is still difficult to understand. (7th)

Refugees from Jiang and Song Regions Seeking Food in Songjiang

Since the beginning of summer this year, drought has ravaged the land, causing severe crop failures in the Zhejiang-Jiaxing area. Some farmers have even experienced total loss of harvest, leading to widespread poverty and desperation. Driven by hunger, people are fleeing their homes with the elderly and young in tow, seeking food in other areas. Recently, refugees from places like Xiashe and Wangdian in Zhejiang-Jiaxing have been arriving in boats, heading towards Qiaoxian County. Hundreds of refugees are lingering around the Jiting, Jiangcang Bridge area in the western suburbs of this city. The county magistrate, Jin Tigan, has initiated relief efforts, collecting donations, and the director of the relief institute, Li Zuhua, along with District Chief Li, are personally distributing aid in the western suburbs, providing each person with one "sheng" of white rice and 200 "wen". The refugees are currently staying in places like the Sanyuan Temple. It is said that the amount distributed has already reached over one hundred yuan. Some are advocating for the establishment of a shelter to fulfill the neighborly duty of disaster relief. Additionally, refugees from Lianshui and Huoqiu counties are passing through this area daily in a continuous stream. The police station is dispatching officers to escort them out of the region.

Opium Addicts Escape from Opium Detoxification Center

Feng Youlu, the director of the county's opium detoxification center, has been managing it for several months, establishing a structured program. Many opium addicts arrested in various townships and districts have been sent to the center for compulsory detoxification. However, on the night of the 9th (yesterday) at around 2 a.m., three opium addicts undergoing detoxification, Gu Fushou, Zhang Zhisan, and Wu Fusheng, escaped from the center. Their whereabouts are currently unknown. Director Feng has submitted a report to the Opium Prohibition Committee, requesting their capture.

Dingjia County Issues Arrest Warrants for Six Former County Magistrates

The provincial government has issued arrest warrants for four former county magistrates of this county, Ma Shaozhou, Chen Chichang, Chen Can, and Shen Tingqi, because their handover of duties was incomplete. Two others, Wu Bogeng and Xing Nan, although they completed the handover, still owe money: Wu owes 3,319 yuan and some change, and Xing owes 1,121 yuan and some change. Despite repeated notices and overdue deadlines, they have ignored the demands and disappeared without a trace. The previous year, a request was submitted to the Executive Yuan to issue arrest warrants for these officials and to confiscate their properties to cover the debts. The Executive Yuan has approved the request and consulted the Judicial Yuan, instructing the Ministry of Judicial Administration to order the Supreme Court Prosecutor's Office to instruct its subordinates to comply.

The Weather in Wuxi is Warm, and Business is Sluggish

In the city, for the past two months, the weather has been warm, with the Fahrenheit thermometer consistently reading between 55 and 56 degrees. This has caused plants to behave abnormally, with bean sprouts flowering out of season. In previous years, business in this period would have already started to improve. However, this year, due to the warm weather and tight credit, commerce has plummeted, with businesses experiencing very few customers, which is unprecedented in recent years. Nevertheless, pre-arranged payments and debts are due on schedule, causing everyone to feel financially strained and unable to close down their businesses.

Provincial Commissioner Arrives in Wuxi to Inspect Land Tax

Zhao Dihua, the Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, recently sent Liu Zhiban, the Head of the First Section, to inspect various counties due to the confusing land tax situation, inconsistent tax rates and regulations, and varying collection procedures. The purpose is to rectify and improve the system. After being dispatched, Liu arrived in Wuxi the day before yesterday and went directly to the county government to meet with Magistrate Yan, inquiring about the political situation. Subsequently, accompanied by Fei Yunong, the Head of the Second Section, Zhu Kaiguan, the Land Tax Director, and Wang Guangyi, the supervising committee member, Liu visited the promotion and collection office for inspection. He then proceeded to inspect the land tax, register, and grain storage offices, and reviewed the prepared tax registration papers. He discovered significant errors and instructed Head Fei to correct them immediately. However, Head Fei explained that the tax registration papers had already been completed, sent for printing, and were scheduled for urgent distribution to complete the tax collection. If corrections were made, the papers would have to be re-edited, which would waste time and require additional expenses, making it difficult to implement. Therefore, he obtained Magistrate Yan's approval to travel to the provincial capital yesterday to request instructions and seek leniency. As a result, the Department of Finance agreed to allow the addition of a stamp on the completed tax registration papers, explaining the deductions. Satisfied with the outcome, Fei returned to the county that evening.

Changshu Party and Government Agencies Hold Discussion Meeting

On the afternoon of the 9th at 2 p.m., various Party and government agencies in the county held a discussion meeting at the county Party headquarters. More than ten leaders from Party and government agencies attended. Wu Ying, the Party Secretary, presided over the meeting, and the following key issues were resolved: (1) It was decided that in the future, Party and government agencies would consult with each other on handling cases involving people's organizations to avoid inconsistencies. (2) The Party and government agencies will jointly organize a charity guidance committee, with the county Party headquarters drafting detailed regulations. (3) The Cotton Yarn Industry Association has insufficient members and does not meet the basic requirements, so its activities should be suspended, and the Party headquarters will send personnel to take over its management. (4) A discussion meeting will be convened with those in charge of the fire brigades in the urban area to discuss improvements in fire control. (5) Regulations for end-of-year good behavior will be established and handled by the New Life Movement Promotion Association.

Changzhou Submits Proposal to Provincial Government to Open City Gate

For the convenience of transportation in the western part of Wuyi County, the county government plans to open a Jingyun Gate in the city wall south of Xiaoshuiguan at the Zhijifang bottom and build a Liufang Bridge outside the city to connect to Taiping Lane outside the West Gate, directly reaching Xinma Road. This would connect with the Zhencheng and Wuyi highways. The Head of the Third Section, Li Jiaji, rushed to prepare the drawings and budget to submit to the Department of Construction for approval. It is rumored that opening the Jingyun Gate will cost approximately over a thousand yuan, which the county government will raise. The funds for building the Liufang Bridge will be raised by local gentry such as Zhuang Zhongxi.

Yanshui and Alcohol License Tax Branch Chief Detained

Zhao Qian, the Branch Chief of the Yanshui and Alcohol License Tax Bureau of Wuyi, Yixing, Xishui, and Yinxian Counties (also known as Zhu Jian, also known as Jinzhang), was discovered by Xie Rentao and others dispatched by the Provincial Bureau at the Changzhou Station on the 8th and immediately taken to the county government for detention. It is rumored that the reason for the detention is that he has been repeatedly accused of using a false name, illegally levying excessive taxes, and failing to remit tax funds. Currently, over six thousand yuan of the autumn tax has been handed over to the Provincial Department. Zhu has requested bail, but the Provincial Bureau must submit a request to the Department of Finance for approval.

Jiangsu-Zhenjiang to Develop Irrigation in Cultivation Area

Jiangsu Province considers the area east of Chanchang River and west of the New Canal as cultivation zone, covering an area of 8,100 square kilometers, equivalent to approximately 13 million mu. Because the area is prone to flooding when the Huai River flows in, taking months to recede, and prone to drought when water sources dry up and saltwater tides flow backward, disasters are frequent. In the past, there were plans to develop the New Canal to seek relief. However, due to the difficult state treasury, it has not been realized. Recently, there are plans to develop irrigation in the cultivation zone. In addition to developing a new canal east of Chanchang River, running north and south for regulation, it is also planned to use the excavated soil to build a large dam on the east bank of the New Canal to prevent the intrusion of sea tides. At the same time, it is planned to build a main road on the west bank to facilitate land transportation, and to dredge ditches west of the New Canal, connecting to Chanchang River to receive water. Canals will be dug east of the New Canal, extending to Xiangkou to facilitate drainage, and sluice gates will be built as appropriate for easy operation. The total cost is estimated at approximately 6.5 million yuan, and planning and preparations are actively underway.

Yangzhou Education Bureau Investigates Embezzlement of Loan Certificates

Jiangdu issued 60,000 yuan of educational loan certificates in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), drawing lots six times in succession, and repaying the principal and interest according to the drawn numbers. Currently, the certificate guarantee committee, because the fund is adequate, has specially changed the original plan of repaying in eight installments to a full repayment. The seventh draw will not take place. However, during the drafting of the full repayment plan, it was discovered that there were cases of only collecting the stamp and not issuing the loan certificate. People in the education sector recalled that during the sixth academic lottery, a delivery worker went to the bureau with a 500-yuan loan certificate to have it stamped, but the bureau suspected that the certificate was questionable and did not stamp it or investigate further. Now that the end is approaching, there are again cases of collecting the stamp but not having the certificate, which is related to the reputation of the education sector and must be investigated. Therefore, it is planned to form an investigation committee to clarify the truth.

Suspect in the Shi Liangcai Case Interrogated Yesterday in Hangzhou

Zhang Wentian, the suspect in the assassination of Mr. Shi Liangcai, was escorted from Shanghai to Hangzhou on the evening of the 8th. Yesterday morning (the 9th) at 9 a.m., Chen Huaming, the prosecutor of the Hangzhou County District Court, opened the trial. The police were ordered to bring the suspect Zhang forward and present a leather bag as evidence. After the prosecutor inquired about his age and origin, he investigated the details of the Shi case in detail. Zhang absolutely denied the matter, claiming complete ignorance and that he had never been to Hangzhou. He admitted that the leather bag belonged to him. The interrogation lasted until around 10 a.m., after which he was ordered to be taken to the detention center for further interrogation.

Bandits from Haining Arrested in Hangzhou

Yu Shunliu, a notorious bandit who has committed multiple crimes in Haining and other counties, was hiding at No. 124 Shijiguan Lane in this city. The joint defense investigation team of the four counties discovered his location and dispatched team members Mao Liheng and Liu Xiang to arrest him at the address and send him to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Jiashan Jiashing Shareholders Clear Outstanding Deposits

The Jiashan Commercial Savings Bank, affected by deposit withdrawals, declared liquidation. Depositors pointed out that the bank's original capital was 500,000 yuan, but only one-quarter of the shares (125,000 yuan) had been paid. Therefore, the creditors' association jointly filed a complaint with the Ministry of Finance. The ministry consulted the Zhejiang Provincial Government, instructing the county to send personnel to conduct a thorough investigation and supervise the liquidation. Now, after receiving a complaint from Xia Weiji and others, the Ministry of Finance issued a directive yesterday, stating that since the bank has publicly announced its liquidation and set a date for repaying debts, it should collect the outstanding capital in full amount within a specified period of time, according to the total capital amount, and liquidate it according to law. The savings deposits should be repaid in full, including principal and interest, according to the current regulations of the Savings Bank Law, with the bank's directors and supervisors jointly and severally liable without limitation, in order to comply with the law and protect the rights of creditors. In addition to the directive, the Ministry of Finance also consulted the Zhejiang Provincial Government to forward it to the Jiashan County Government for handling and requested that the handling situation be reported to the ministry for verification.

Special Article

A Review of the World Economy in 1934 (Continued) - Mu Ouchu

The prosperity of the fuel and electrical industries further proves the development of the military industry. Fuel is mainly coal and kerosene. The world coal production in the first half of 1934 is listed as follows:

World Coal Production (Unit: 1,000 tons)

First Half of 1932: 449,530

Second Half of 1932: 460,791

First Half of 1933: 448,910

Second Half of 1933: 501,515

January 1934: 94,315

February 1934: 88,202

March 1934: 98,683

April 1934: 80,439

May 1934: 83,499

June 1934: 80,525

Total for First Half: 525,563

(Source: League of Nations Survey)

Although the coal production in the first half of 1934 showed a slight recovery compared to the previous two years, it was still lower than the production of 1.3 billion tons in 1929. However, this does not mean that fuel consumption decreased, because kerosene is gradually replacing coal. Although statistics on world kerosene production in 1934 have not been found, 1933 already had a new record. Kerosene production in 1934 was certainly not lower than the previous year but had an increasing trend. The comparison of kerosene production in the past 20 years is as follows:

(Source: British Petroleum Association Survey, Unit: Million Tons)

1913: 53.7

1928: 124.2

1929: 206.7

1930: 196.8

1931: 189.7

1932: 179.3

1933: 194.3

Among the driving forces, due to electrification, all countries are striving to develop power. Therefore, the increase in the production and consumption of electricity can also prove the development of the military industry. In the United States, the first half of 1934 increased compared to the previous two years. U.S. Electricity Production and Consumption Index

Monthly Average Production Consumption

1932 70.9 87.5

1933 84.9 87.5

1934 94.1 107.1

(Source: League of Nations Survey, the consumption index is based on the average of 1923-1925 as 100, and the production index is based on the estimated level as 100. Because the standards are different, the comparison of growth and decline cannot be made. Only the production and consumption can be compared separately.)

Shipping Industry: Due to the shrinkage of international trade in the past few years, the shipping industry in various countries has gradually declined. However, in the second half of 1933, it gradually showed signs of improvement. In 1934, this phenomenon continued to be maintained. The statistics of the number of ships under construction in the world in 1934 was 1,079,100 tons, an increase of 321,800 tons compared to the end of 1933. The increase rate was the largest in the United States. Last year, it increased about twice as much as the same period last year. At the end of March of the year before last, there were only 252,000 tons, but this year it has increased to 481,000 tons, accounting for almost half of the world's total. Except for England, the rest of the world is 597,000 tons; among them, Japan also increased by 16,000 tons in March last year compared with the same period last year, and other countries such as Germany, France, the United States, and the Netherlands also had considerable increases.

Automobile Industry: In 1933, the world's production volume was already considerable. In 1932, the world produced a total of 1,977,000 vehicles, and in 1933 it increased to 2,672,000 vehicles. The United States alone increased by 588,000 vehicles in one year (League of Nations Survey). After the start of 1934, it increased even more sharply. In the first three months alone, the United States produced 732,100 vehicles, an increase of about 60% compared to the same period last year. The production volume of British automobiles surprisingly broke the unprecedented record in 1933, reaching 286,000 vehicles; the Soviet Union produced a total of 16,073 vehicles in the first half of 1934, which also showed a clear increase compared to the same period last year. (Cultural Construction, Volume 1, Issue 3, pages 78)

The structure of automobiles has the latest equipment, which can be quickly converted into tanks. This is worth noting. Although we cannot deny that the transportation industry has made considerable progress in 1934, it is undeniable that the development of the automobile industry is mostly for the preparation of war.

According to the general principles of economics, increased production must be accompanied by increased trade. However, the world trade in 1934 was inversely proportional to world production, which can also prove that the contradiction between production and consumption has not disappeared at all. The comparison of world trade in the first half of 1934 with the previous two years is as follows:

Import Export

First Half of 1932 6,661 5,841

Second Half of 1932 6,195 5,415

First Half of 1933 5,950 5,415

Second Half of 1933 6,035 5,762

January 1934 983 895

February 1934 898 855

March 1934 1,001 961

April 1934 955 847

May 1934 981 874

June 1934 959 879

July 1934 896 838

(Unit: Million Gold Dollars, League of Nations Survey)

The import in the first half of 1934 was about 5.8 billion gold dollars, and the export was about 5.3 billion gold dollars, both showing a reduction. This is in terms of the world. As for the countries, there are quite different points. The foreign trade of the major countries is listed as follows:

1932 1933 1934

Import 361 341 320 356 362

Germany Million Marks Export 2,989 2,751 2,378 2,494 2,086

(Source: Japanese News Agency, "Where is the World Going", Second Half of 1934, page 84)

The decrease in exports from Germany, France, and Italy is a sacrifice for maintaining the value of currencies in the gold standard countries, while the import and export of countries that implement currency inflation, such as the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan, are gradually increasing. Therefore, the gold standard countries are more self-conscious. At the same time, we can see the sharpening of the confrontation between the powers. This sharpening is the fuse of the Second World War.

The development of economic panic not only caused panic in agriculture and industry at the same time, but also intertwined the two, making the panic enter a dangerous situation. The panic that occurred in 1929 was the prelude to the intertwining of the two; this panic continued until 1934.

Agricultural production in 1934 did not improve, although it had a great relationship with unfavorable climate, but most of it was due to the agricultural panic. The production of major raw materials is listed as follows:

Cotton Raw Silk Wool

There are international production reduction agreements on sugar production, but there is still an increasing phenomenon. An international production reduction agreement was also established on rubber on April 29, 1934, restricting the global production volume to no more than 1,019,000 tons. After June, there was a certain ratio to gradually reduce production to avoid the risk of overproduction. The production reduction agreement is a last resort during the panic period. The fact that this phenomenon occurred in 1934 clearly shows that 1934 was still in the deep vortex of panic.

Agricultural panic can also be proven by the drop in agricultural product prices. For example, the drop in orchid prices in Japan is very impressive.

Powell Lectures on the Recent Situations of Russia and Japan

According to the Continental Press, Mr. Powell, editor of the China Weekly Review, recently traveled to Japan, Northeast China, and Soviet Russia. Yesterday afternoon (the 9th), at the Bankers' Association, he shared his observations from his travels with members and friends of the China International Problems Research Association. He stated that Japan is in a state of political anxiety and hesitation, while Soviet Russia is engaged in the orderly development of heavy industry, building a railway network, and pushing its military bases towards Vladivostok in order to seize economic hegemony on its far eastern border. However, it is still striving for peace, as its purpose is to defend its Pacific coast. Japan's anxiety stems from a deep belief that in a future Far Eastern war, the United States and Russia will form an economic alliance to resist Japan, and that both countries are hidden dangers for Japan. Therefore, it adopts a tough, unpredictable attitude towards Russia, the United States, and China. In recent years, Japan's war industry has profited the most, followed by the chemical industry. Last year, more than 300 Japanese arms dealers averaged profits of more than 12%. However, 50% of the country's income is actually monopolized by the warlords. Japan is now forcibly subjecting strong young men in rural areas and elsewhere to military training for a certain period of time. The difficulty lies in the fact that after the training, there is no way to allow them to return to farming. This problem is very serious, and both the military and political circles are deeply worried. Turning to Fascism is actually the only way for Japan to handle state affairs today. There are many Chinese people in the Soviet Russian secret detective teams, especially in Vladivostok. There are 10,000 overseas Chinese in that area and the Lake Baikal region. From a transportation point of view, China is geographically isolated from Soviet Russia, as now going from China to Russia requires passing through the puppet state of Manchukuo forcibly occupied by the Japanese. The military and industrial programs stipulated in the Soviet Russian second five-year plan are proceeding very quickly. Soviet Russian industries are now secretly assisted by the army, especially in the area from the Ural Mountains to the Pacific coast. According to foreign military attachés, the Soviet Russian mechanized army is the most powerful in the world. All strong young men aged 22 must undergo military training for two to six years, from infantry drills to driving tanks and airplanes. A total of 1.5 million people are recruited for testing, and more than 300,000 have now been selected for enlistment. Soviet Russia is no longer as actively engaged in communist propaganda abroad as before. Soviet Russian officials believe that the strength of the military is already strong, so this kind of propaganda is no longer necessary. Therefore, they have now retreated to studying national defense. Soviet Russia is determined to defend the land along the Pacific coast, including the Vladivostok military port, because in the event of war, it can self-supply military needs and agricultural products without relying on Moscow. Last year, 2,000 tons of oil were produced in the northern corner of Sakhalin. Soviet Russia hopes that production can increase to 800,000 tons by 1937, so that it can protect the area with oil production. The Soviet Russian industrial program stipulates that Khabarovsk is the metropolis of the Far East, Chita is the metropolis of East Siberia, and Novosibirsk is the metropolis of South Siberia. Novosibirsk is the intersection of the Turkestan-Siberian Railway. Xinjiang's products are all exported through this route, so it is becoming increasingly important. Soviet Russian officials all believe that Xinjiang's fur trade and other products will inevitably use Novosibirsk as a distribution center in the future, and Xinjiang will rely on this export economically. Direct transportation between China and Xinjiang is difficult, so China is afraid that it will be difficult to maintain the province. The railway between Chita and the North Amur River is currently being laid and its track is being changed. A new railway is currently being built from Irkutsk to Lake Baikal to consolidate the region's economic development and to quickly transport troops in times of war. However, Soviet Russian farmers lack the mechanical knowledge necessary to manage industrial development. This is a major problem for Soviet Russia's transition from an agricultural country to an industrial country. The theoretically advocated wage equality is actually difficult to implement, because experienced workers naturally need to be paid higher wages than ordinary workers. Soviet Russian industrialized factories are now managed jointly by a national committee member, a party member, and a trade union leader. The housing problem in Soviet Russian cities is also one of the most difficult to solve. Although the government has built residential houses, it still cannot solve the problem of crowding in the city. The Japanese government, in view of Soviet Russia's ambitious operations, is now economically united with the puppet state of Manchukuo, building trunk roads to cut off the transportation between Vladivostok and Soviet Russia, and to make Vladivostok rely on Japan rather than Siberia. Japan is currently carrying out a "heavy industry program" in the puppet state of Manchukuo, believing that if it is short of pig iron supply, it will lose its important power as an industrial country. In recent years, Japan has been the largest market in the world for buying scrap iron. It is now planning to open iron mines in the puppet state of Manchukuo so that it will no longer rely on the world.

Ministry of Finance Facilitates the Flow of Silver Between the Interior and Coastal Areas

Yesterday Instructed the Silver and Money Trades Associations

To Temporarily Suspend the Implementation of the Fourth Measure for Obtaining Licenses

The Ministry of Finance instructed the Shanghai Banking and Money Trades Associations yesterday, saying, "The requirement to apply for passports for transporting cash is originally intended to prevent the smuggling of goods for export. The Ministry had previously stipulated that the old licensing measures were limited to banks applying, and ordinary merchants were not allowed to use them. In addition, the passports were only issued by the Ministry, which was very inconvenient in remote areas. In consideration of the business situation, some flexibility was given, and five licensing measures were prescribed to facilitate matters. These measures have already been communicated separately. Now, according to previous reports, in this period of major settlement, the inland transport and trade is frequent and should be facilitated to avoid delaying opportunities. It is now provisionally approved that, except for the coastal and border areas where cash transport requires licensing in accordance with the original five measures, all inland cash transport shall temporarily suspend the implementation of the original fourth measure, in order to show the utmost consideration for the business situation. In addition to separate consultations, it is hereby ordered that the association shall transmit the order to all its member firms for compliance. This is the order."

Silver to be Shipped to Shanghai will be Deposited in Three Banks for Financial Regulation

The Foreign Exchange Rate Fell to 28 Cents and has Returned to Normal

According to the New Sound News Agency, the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee has entrusted the Central Bank to purchase 20 million yuan of silver from Hong Kong. After the procedures are completed, it will be shipped to Shanghai in two batches. The first batch of 10 million yuan will be loaded onto a special ship in Hong Kong and shipped to Shanghai immediately, scheduled to arrive in Shanghai next week. For the sake of prudence, the special ship will not carry passengers except for the silver. At the same time, police will be sent to protect the ship. The date of loading the second batch is expected to be within the next week, and it is expected to arrive completely before the settlement of accounts for various industries.

To be Deposited in Three Banks

According to a reporter from the New Sound News Agency who inquired with banking circles, after the silver arrives in Shanghai, it will be deposited in the Central, China, and Communications Banks for financial regulation. The funds designated by the above three banks are related to the mortgage loans for the silver and money trades, because it is deeply feared that if the Shanghai market experiences a cash crunch during the year-end settlement, this silver will be used as a mortgage loan for the silver and money trades as a precautionary measure. The purpose is to stabilize the market.

Credit Conditions Gradually Easing

Since the funds designated by the Central, China, and Communications Banks for mortgage loans for the silver and money trades, and the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee's purchase of silver and its shipment to Shanghai for regulation, credit conditions in Shanghai have gradually eased. The "yang chai" used in the money market has fallen from a peak of 60 cents to 35 cents. The opening market prices yesterday morning and afternoon fell to 28 cents, and have returned to normal.

Articles of Association and List of Members of the Monetary System Committee

Researching Countermeasures to Gold and Silver Issues

According to the National News Agency, the Ministry of Finance's Monetary System Research Committee was established in Nanjing last winter, and a Shanghai office was set up at the end of last year. However, the articles of association and the list of all the committee members have not yet been announced to the public. They are now published as follows:

Articles of Association

"Articles of Association of the Monetary System Research Committee of the Ministry of Finance" (Article 1) The Ministry of Finance has specially established the Monetary System Research Committee to study matters related to monetary system reform. (Article 2) The Monetary System Research Committee shall have a number of members, who shall be selected and appointed by the Minister of Finance, and one of the members shall be designated as the chairman. (Article 3) The meetings of the Monetary System Research Committee shall be presided over by the chairman. (Article 4) The Monetary System Research Committee shall have one secretary-general, two secretaries, and a number of clerks, who shall be dispatched by the Minister of Finance. (Article 5) The matters to be studied by the Monetary System Research Committee are as follows: (1) Matters relating to the adoption of the gold standard; (2) Matters relating to the silver standard currency; (3) Matters relating to various old currencies; (4) Matters relating to subsidiary coins; (5) Matters relating to the prohibition of private minting; (6) Matters relating to the improvement of mints; (7) Matters relating to the transport and regulation of silver and copper yuan in various places; (8) Matters relating to paper money; (9) Matters relating to the prohibition of private issuance of paper money; (10) Matters referred by the Minister of Finance for discussion. (Article 6) The members of the Monetary System Research Committee may raise issues for discussion on all matters listed in Article 5. (Article 7) The resolutions of the Monetary System Research Committee shall be submitted to the Minister of Finance for adoption and implementation. (Article 8) The detailed rules for the Monetary System Research Committee shall be formulated separately. (Article 9) These Articles of Association shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

List of Committee Members

Chen Jintao (concurrently Chairman), Zhang Jia'ao (public), Wu Dingchang (Daquan), Qian Yongming (Xinzhi), Zhou Zuomin, Chen Huide (Guangfu), Bei Zuyi (Songsun), Hu Yun (Bijiang), Tang Daomin, Song Ziliang, Hu Zutong (Mengjia), Shen Yuanding (Laiqing), Qu Zihui (Jigang), Xu Xinliu, Qin Zuze (Runqing), Geng Aide, E. Kann, Sun Hengfu, Fu Zongyao (Xiaoan), Qi Zhi (Yunqing), Bian Baimei, Wu Zhenxiu, Ye Dong (Fuxiao), Wu Yunzhai, Gu Jigao, Yu Fengshao (Huancheng), Liu Dajun (Jitao), Zeng Rongpu (Zongjian), Li Jue, Chen Duan, Lu Xuepu (Jianquan), Dai Mingli (Lian'an, concurrently Secretary), Chen Xing (Jian'an), Xi Demao, Shen Shuyu, Tao Dekun (Zhonghan, concurrently Secretary), Xu Kan (Keting), Wu Zengyu (Jiezhi), Yang Qiguan (Ziyuan, concurrently Secretary).

Setting up an Office

The Ministry of Finance added a Shanghai office because most of the committee members were in Shanghai on official business. The office was intended to serve two purposes: to facilitate communication and to allow members to fully utilize the library of the Central Bank for consultation of global economic books and newspapers. The study of global monetary systems and silver and gold issues would also provide the committee ample resources for discussion during meetings. The meeting decisions would then be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval per the committee's charter's Article 7.

Meeting Period

The committee has decided to hold two meetings annually which will be convened in Nanjing. The exact dates for future meetings have not been set. The committee believes that the international economic tides are ever-changing, and in order to regulate the nation's monetary system, the domestic policies must adapt to that current. Failure to do so is to focus on the trivial and not address critical needs. For this reason, the committee is currently researching strategies to address the silver and gold questions. As soon as there is progress, proposed plans will be drafted and explored.

The yearbook is an indispensable and important reference book for modern life. When dealing with matters, they need to examine regulations and review the status of politics, law, finance, finance, transportation, production, education, culture, and society. All of these can be found in it. The Shen Bao Yearbook, compiled and published by the Shen Bao, has been published twice and has become popular throughout the country. Those who have purchased it from all walks of life have praised its rich content and practicality. Now, the third revision is being carried out, and more "new," "refined," and "accurate" practical materials are being widely collected, and experts are being invited to write manuscripts by category, in the hope that the domestic knowledge class and those who handle public and private affairs can place this book on their desks and apply it infinitely, without feeling the lack of practical knowledge. The pre-order method for the book can be announced in the advertisement of this newspaper. According to the person in charge of the Shen Bao Yearbook, the third yearbook is to commemorate the founder, Mr. Shi Liangcai. In addition to striving for progress in content, the pre-order price is also specially reduced in order to popularize it, and it is hoped that 50,000 pre-order subscribers can be obtained.

Middle Cabin Workers Humiliated and Committed Suicide, All Employees of the Shipping Lines Jointly Request Negotiation

Yesterday, a petition was made to the Seamen's Union for assistance.

According to Dagong News Agency, Tong Tianhou, a middle cabin worker on the Xianghe, which is operated by the British company Jardine Matheson on the Yangtze River route, failed to board the ship because it started early. Therefore, he transferred to the Longhe to catch up and planned to board the ship in Nanjing. However, the comprador of the Longhe, a Westerner named Newman, forced him to buy a ticket because he was boarding the ship without a ticket. The worker pleaded to buy a half-price ticket (from Shanghai to Beijing) because he had no money. However, after the ship arrived in Beijing, he still failed to catch up with the Xianghe. When he returned to Shanghai on the original ship, the comprador forced him to buy a ticket again and beat and humiliated him. Overwhelmed with resentment, the worker committed suicide by jumping into the river when the ship arrived in Wuhu. The body was examined by the Wuhu Local Court, which proved that he had suffered serious injuries and committed suicide by jumping into the river. Now, the middle cabin workers of various shipping companies under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai Middle Cabin Office, including China Merchants, Nissin, Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Datong, and Dada, were outraged when they heard about the incident. They believed that the Westerner deliberately abused Chinese workers. They had gathered several times to decide to organize a support association to conduct negotiations. Yesterday, Wang Oumin, a member of the Middle Cabin Office, was sent to the Chinese Seamen's Union to petition for assistance. Secretary Sun Luping received him and promised to collect evidence immediately and conduct negotiations. The workers believed that the matter was of international concern and would invite the press to report the incident within a few days and ask them to uphold justice in order to seek redress.

Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Lawyers' Association

The 187th Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association held its 187th joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees at its office at No. 572, intersection of Beiler Road and Lafayette Road in the French Concession at 7 pm last night. The committee members who attended were Shen Junru, Hu Jue, Zhu Fuju, Ma Junshuo, Li Ming, Chen Zhigao, Zhou Xiaoan, Mao Yun, Wang Weizhen, Zhang Zhengxue, Yang Zhihao, etc. Shen Junru was elected as chairman, and Dai Jiguang was the recorder. The meeting was held as usual. The proposals are recorded as follows: (1) A case of a telegram from the Minister of Judicial Administration thanking him for his congratulations; (2) Regarding the Lawyers' Association's joint proposal to the Ministry of Judicial Administration that lawyers should be allowed to participate in judicial conferences, the case was temporarily suspended because the Minister had just taken office; (3) The Shanghai Local Court ordered the improvement of the time for meeting with prisoners in the detention center, and the case has been ordered to be improved; (4) Shi Zechen reported on the preparations for the establishment of the Fourth Branch of the Jiangsu High Court; (5) A letter from the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation replied to the Shanghai Local Court's request for a solution to the problem of lawyers taking a rest and having telephone calls answered in the concession. The above five cases were "resolved" and filed for future reference. (6) Lu Shaozong, Wu Guochang, Ye Xiabiao, Zhu Shuzhen, Gu Xianzhang, Xu Xingti, and other members also engaged in business, which did not hinder their duties as lawyers. Cases were sent to seek permission respectively. It was resolved that, except for Gu Xianzhang, who collected debts on behalf of others, which was a matter within the duties of the members and did not need to be discussed, the rest were approved and allowed to engage in both. (7) The Wuxian Lawyers' Association sent a letter informing that the Jiangsu Higher Court agreed to the expenses of the defender's carriage and horses, which should be borne by the Shanghai, Wuxian, Zhenjiang, Jiangning, Wujin, Wuxi, Nantong, Songjiang, and Jiangdu associations in accordance with the number of members. It was resolved that since this carriage and horse fee is borne by the associations, the associations should be the unit. Moreover, the number of members is not fixed, and the number of members should not be used as the standard for the associations to bear the expenses. A letter was sent to reply that each association should still bear the expenses equally. (8) Former member Shen Yuesheng absconded due to debt and sent the cases he handled back to the association for safekeeping and handling. After the association entrusted lawyer Zhao Zuwei and an accountant to sort them out first, lawyer Zhao replied that lawyer Shen Yuesheng had embezzled more than 55,000 yuan from the parties, which could not be dealt with. Please approve the method; (9) Chen Hansen reported that lawyer Shen Yuesheng had paid a 10,000 yuan bond in public debt and asked the lawyer in charge to collect it; (10) Dunxu Bank reported that lawyer Shen Yuesheng had embezzled 2,000 taels of bond and asked for justice; (11) The Book Purchasing Committee of the Association reported on the review of lawyer Shen Yuesheng's collection of books. The above four cases were discussed together and resolved: (A) A letter was sent to lawyer Zhao Zuwei stating that the association had no right to take over the case and that the creditors should organize a creditors' group to handle it; (B) The books collected by member Shen should still be requested to be returned by the original handler; (C) The letters from Chen Hansen and Dunxu Bank should be replied to for self-negotiation; (12) Lawyer Liu Bin sent a letter reporting that the sentence of imprisonment had been revoked and changed to a fine, which had been determined, and requested to restore membership. It was resolved that he was allowed to restore membership; (13) Member Chen Bingxuan sent a letter requesting an explanation of Shanghai's habit of being beneficial to tenants. It was resolved that an investigation and reply should be made; (14) The National Electrical Undertakings Guidance Association of the Construction Association sent a draft of the regulations for cracking down on stealing water and electricity, soliciting opinions. It was resolved that Zhang Zhengxue and Guo Shouyi should be appointed to review it; (15) The Shanghai Tongzhi Museum sent a letter requesting the investigation and filling in of the Shanghai Twenty-Three Yearbook survey data. It was resolved that Wu should handle it; (16) The chairman reported on the establishment of the affiliated Poor People's Legal Aid Association and requested an appropriation for office expenses. It was resolved that the necessary expenses for the association's office would be paid by the association; (17) The association's final accounts for the second half of the twenty-third year were submitted for review and whether they should be reviewed by an accountant. It was resolved that they should be passed and sent to accountant Zhao Zuwei for review; (18) Lawyers Wang Maolin, Xia Yifeng, Qian Zonghua, Gu Peilun, Ma Pingxun, Chen Haisen, Yin Fubao, Xue Jiguang, etc. applied for membership. It was resolved that they were passed. The meeting adjourned after the agenda was completed, as it was already late at night.

Daxing Company's New Hongxing Ship to Make Maiden Voyage to Ningbo

Costing More Than 300,000 Yuan, with New Equipment

And Planning to Invite People from All Walks of Life to Visit

This port's Daxing Shipping Company's original Hongxing ship, which runs the Shanghai-Ningbo route, is relatively small and has insufficient cabin space. Therefore, in October of the year before last, it set up the Hongchang Shipyard to add a new ship, named New Hongxing. The reporter of China News Agency learned that the ship was launched at the end of last month and is docked at the Daxing Pier on South City Outer Bund. It has been testing its engine on the Huangpu River for days and testing its speed. The ship is 22 feet long, 35 feet wide, and has a deep draft. It can travel about 13 nautical miles per hour. The ship's body is the same as the Ningbo style, but larger than the original Hongxing. It has three decks, more than 50 official cabins, first, second, and third class berths, and all the cabins. The total cost is more than 300,000 yuan, and the equipment is new. It is now actively arranging everything. It is said that the ship is scheduled to depart from Shanghai to Ningbo this Friday or Saturday, and it is also planned to invite people from all walks of life to visit. During the maiden voyage, all passengers on the ship will receive gifts. Once the new ship is put into service, the old Hongxing ship will be put into dock for repairs, and it has not yet been decided where it will be rerouted in the future.

The Bureau of Works Modifies the Well Water Inspection Rules

The Bureau of Works recently slightly modified Article 7 of the Bylaws on Self-Flowing Well Licenses, that is, Bureau officials may take water samples from the well at any time and shall not be prevented from doing so. If the results of the initial formal inspection are satisfactory, no further fees will be charged for taking samples for inspection in the future. If the initial inspection fails, the Bureau may charge a handling fee for re-inspection.

Rice Boats Docking at Foreign Wharf to Temporarily Maintain the Status Quo Within the Past Few Years

Considering the Livelihood of the Workers

Discussing Methods Afterwards

More than 200 shoulder-carrying laborers from the foreign banks on the Wusong River petitioned the United Association of Rice Merchants in Northern Shanghai because the rice merchants of various gangs decided that all the rice and grain on the bank should be stopped from docking at the foreign bank wharf due to the danger of arranging ships. They requested that the current situation be maintained, considering the livelihood of the workers, but it was not approved. The shoulder-carrying laborers went to petition again yesterday, requesting that they temporarily continue to dock at the foreign bank wharf within the past few years, and then discuss concrete methods. The rice merchants, considering the livelihood of the workers, have agreed to temporarily arrange ships as before during the Lunar New Year.

Zhabei Gruel Kitchen Continues to Open

Another New Site Added, Accommodating 6,000 People

Since the second gruel kitchen on Liuying Road, which is sponsored by the Zhabei Charity Group, opened on the 1st of this month, the number of poor people going to the kitchen for food has been increasing day by day, with about 15,000 people per day. Therefore, the kitchen was insufficient in capacity and was temporarily closed on the 15th of this month. Wang Binyan, the director of the group, urgently sought follow-up methods and immediately convened a board meeting to decide to not only raise donations from the directors, but also solicit donations from other charitable organizations and philanthropists in order to continue the gruel distribution. Since the closure of the kitchen, it has attracted the attention of people from all walks of life. The reporter of China Eastern News Agency went to the kitchen yesterday to investigate. The kitchen covers an area of about 7 acres and is covered with reed sheds. There are four kitchens in the east, west, south, and north inside the gate, which can cook 48 pots of gruel. Each day requires 32 stones of rice. If it is still not enough, copper coins will be issued, 9 for large mouths and 6 for small mouths. From the 1st to the 4th of this month, a total of 450,000 coins were issued, but it was still increasing day by day, making it difficult to maintain. Therefore, it was temporarily announced that the distribution would be suspended from the 5th. Wang is now planning to restore the kitchen and hired workers to add a kitchen to the east side of the kitchen the day before yesterday, which can accommodate more than 6,000 poor people. Coal stoves will be added to cook more than 10 pots of gruel, which will be completed in a few days and will continue to be open to benefit the poor.

Zhejiang Elder Zhang Danting Passed Away

Zhang Danting, a well-respected elder in Zhejiang, passed away in his hometown of Huangyan at the age of 74. Friends in Shanghai and fellow villagers in Zhejiang and Taiwan plan to hold a memorial service. Zhang's name is Liansheng, and his courtesy name is Danting. He was from Huangyan County, Zhejiang. He joined the Zhejiang Tibiao Right Camp as a child and was promoted to captain due to his merits. When the Sino-Japanese War broke out, he asked to lead a team north to resist Japan. After the war, he served as the Zhen of Huzhou, Jiaza, Pingyang, and other towns in Zhejiang, and served as the commander of the Dinghai Zhen in Zhejiang twice. He was awarded the title of Zhenwei General and concurrently served as the commander of the Zhejiang Northern Route. At that time, the bandits in Zhejiang disappeared, and the people of the land still praised him. The following year, he was ordered to establish a police academy in Ningbo and served as the director. Therefore, most of the police chiefs came from his school. During the Xinhai Revolution, he happened to be in Suzhou and served as the commander of the Suzhou-Zhejiang Shallow Water Warship. He was the first to contact the various armies to revolt, and commanded the Jiangsu Xuanfeng Brigade and eight shallow water warships to assist the Zhejiang army in recovering Nanjing. He returned to the sea in the fourth year of the Republic of China to handle charitable affairs, such as the Chinese and Foreign Charity Accounts Association and the Zhejiang and Taiwan Six County Flood Disaster Association, saving the victims of the disaster, which was a great contribution.

Manulife Insurance Establishes Chinese Department

Manulife Financial, one of the world's largest life insurance companies, was founded in 1887 and is headquartered in Toronto, Canada, with total assets exceeding US$100 million. It has established a branch in China for 40 years. There are a large number of important figures in the political and business circles of China who have taken out huge life insurance policies in the company, but the majority of the company's policyholders are still Westerners. It is recently learned that the company has added a Chinese department in order to promote its Chinese business. It has now been organized and has hired Mr. Shen Zonglian as the Chinese manager. Mr. Shen has a master's degree in economics from Harvard University in the United States and has served in the Ministry of Finance for many years. He is knowledgeable and experienced. His appointment as the manager of the company this time will definitely make a great contribution. It is also learned that Mr. Shen has written a book on the principles of insurance, which will be published soon.

Municipal Finance Bureau Starts Collecting Land Price Tax in Two Districts

Collection begins on February 1.

Deadline for Completion Within Two Months

Cai Zengji, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, issued Public Notice No. 279 yesterday regarding the collection of the second installment of the land price tax for the 23rd year in the Zhabei and Yangjing districts. It is hereby announced that the second installment of the provisional land price tax for the 23rd year, which should be collected in the Zhabei District, including the desolated character of the second map, the Ze, Chen, Su, and Lie characters of the fourth map, the Zhang and Han characters of the fifth map, the Shu and Wang characters of the sixth map, and the second, third, fifth, and sixth maps of the Yangjing District, will be collected from February 1 of this year. From the date of collection, the deadline for completion is within two months, until March 31 of this year. Those whose land is in the Zhabei District should bring their receipts from the previous period and pay at the North Shanghai Collection Office of the Bureau on Datong Road in Zhabei. Those whose land is in the Yangjing District should bring their receipts from the previous period and pay at the East Shanghai Collection Office of the Bureau at Chunjiang Pier in Pudong. Those who fail to pay within the time limit will be pursued in accordance with Article 8 of the Provisional Land Price Tax Collection Regulations and Article 23 of the Implementation Rules, and an annual interest will be added to the amount owed, and the income from the land will be extracted and auctioned off in proportion to the number of years in arrears, in order to comply with the regulations and emphasize tax revenue. In addition to reporting to the municipal government and sending a notice, it is hereby issued as a public notice, so that taxpayers can abide by it and complete the payment within the time limit, without delay, so as not to incur punishment. If the notice has not yet been received, the location of the land, the map number, and the current address or mailing address should be provided to the Bureau within the time limit for clarification and re-delivery of the duplicate, while still relying on the same receipt from the previous period to complete the payment, without making a mistake. This is the public notice.

Continued Trial of the Mrs. Yu Case Kidnapping

Yu He Zhenya, a Cantonese woman residing in a Western-style house at No. 60, Xi'ai Xiansi Road, in the French Concession, was riding in a chartered car to the Catholic Church on Luban Road to attend Mass at 8 am on October 21 last year. When she arrived near the Gao San Branch School on Xi'ai Xiansi Road, she was suddenly kidnapped by bandits who demanded a huge ransom. The ransom was negotiated in Suzhou. On November 19, the French police arrested six men and women, including the kidnappers Wang Fukang, Lin De, Tao Shuigen, Zhang Huizhi, Zhou Juqin, and the suspect Li Chunxiao, in Suzhou and Shanghai. The hostage was rescued, and two guns were seized. At the same time, Zhang Chunsheng, a 47th-class detective, was shot and injured in the left knee by the bandits when he was resisting arrest. The two bandits, Tong Lin and Tao, seeing the danger, shot themselves and injured themselves. They were sent to the hospital by the police for treatment. Tao died of his injuries, and Lin recovered after 50 days of treatment. He was brought back by the police for further investigation. The investigation was concluded, and they were sent to the Special Second Court on the 8th of this month for prosecution in accordance with Article 1, Paragraph 1 of the Regulations on Punishing Bandits. The Lin bandit was also prosecuted for attempted murder. After Judge Xiong Huiping held a trial and questioned them separately, the trial was adjourned to another date due to lack of time. Yesterday afternoon, a special court was held for the continued trial. The details have been recorded in the newspaper on the 9th of this month. At 3 pm yesterday, Judge Xiong, accompanied by Secretary Tao, specially opened the second criminal court to continue the trial. Lawyer Gu Shouxi appeared in court on behalf of the Police Department. Li Chunxiao, one of the defendants, hired lawyer Li Ming to defend him. The defendants were still questioned separately. The testimonies of the defendants were the same as those given on the 9th, so they will not be repeated here. Then, the witness, the second landlord of the ticket hiding agency at No. 368, Yulin Road, was called to the stand. According to the testimony, the house was rented by Lin De and Zhou Juqin, and the rent was paid by Lin De. The coachman of the affected car and the gate guard of Gao San Branch School were also called to the stand for questioning. According to the coachman, someone pressed the back of the car canopy at that time, and my body was lifted up by the car, my feet were off the ground, and several people came up, lifted Mrs. Yu into the car, and escaped. I could not remember the faces of the bandits at the scene. After the bandits were arrested, the police ordered me to pull the car to the scene of the incident, and when the bandits demonstrated the kidnapping, I saw these two people (referring to Wang Fukang and Lin De) and recognized their faces. The gate guard of Gao San Branch School said that the scene of the incident was about 10 meters away from my post. I only heard screams for help and could not recognize the faces. At this point, the court adjourned the trial to the 24th because the victim, Yu He Zhenya, had not arrived. The defendants were still sent back to prison separately. However, Li Chunxiao was allowed to be transferred to the detention center at the request of his defense lawyer, but visits were prohibited. It is also heard that Li runs a shop in Suzhou and has a wife and children in Suzhou. He met Wang Fukang outside the Panmen gate and sent him to the train station, and was arrested together at the station. The result of the trial will be revealed in the future, but from this, we can see that we must be careful when making friends.

Shanghai-Songjiang Bus and Truck Collide at Maojiawan Yesterday Morning

A total of five people were injured.

The Shanghai-Songjiang Long-Distance Bus Company sent driver Chen Quangen to drive the No. 3 bus from Songjiang to Shanghai at 7:30 yesterday morning. At 8:20, the bus passed Maojiawan, east of the Zhuanqiao Station on the Shanghai-Minhang South Zha Road. Suddenly, Wu Bangping, a driver from the Ruifeng Freight Company in Lujiabang, driving truck No. 13271, which was loaded with six electric poles and two water-mud covers from the Huashang Electric Company, and eight or nine workers, came head-on. At that time, the fog was thick, and it was difficult to see people. Although the truck was not running at full speed, it was in the middle of the road, and it was difficult for Chen to avoid it, resulting in a violent collision between the two vehicles. With a bang, the cylinders and glass of both vehicles were shattered, and the machines were completely damaged. Chen Quangen injured his right hand, and passengers Li Weixian (from Songjiang) and He Yunfu (from Shanghai) injured their heads and faces. They were sent to the Southeast Hospital by the Shanghai-Minhang Company for treatment. Fortunately, the injuries were not serious. After bandaging, they were discharged from the hospital. The rest went to see a doctor themselves. Three workers on the truck were also injured by the shock and were sent to the Shanghai Hospital by the Xiqu Fire Brigade.

Case of a Money Shop Manager Misappropriating Funds

The Jiukang Money Shop, located at No. 110 Beihai Road, has a capital of 14,000 yuan and is managed by Gong Chongzhong from Zhejiang and Xu Zhenting from Jiangyin.

Tang Jianting from Nanjing is the accountant, and Wang Changsheng is the supervisor. Gong and others each held one or two shares. On the first of this month, Wang Changsheng went to the Jiukang Money Shop to audit the accounts and discovered that Gong and the other two had embezzled 17,205 yuan of public funds. He reported this to the Old Gate Police Station, which ordered detective Weng Hongxun to arrest Gong and the others and hand them over to the First Special District Local Court for interrogation and detention, as previously reported in detail. Yesterday morning, Qian Hongye, the criminal division chief of the First Special Court, opened a first criminal court to re-examine the case. The three defendants hired lawyer E Sen for their defense. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, presented the case, prosecuting them for embezzlement under Article 357 of the Criminal Law. Subsequently, Gao Danhua, the plaintiff's representative, stated that the private suit portion had been settled, so he requested that the attached civil suit be withdrawn. When questioned, the defendants all confessed that because their salaries were low and the cost of living was high, they had to temporarily take the money. They claimed this was a common practice in the money shop industry, a kind of partner's debt. The court, recognizing that the facts were clear, ordered the start of the debate. After mutual arguments between the police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, and lawyer E Sen, lawyer E Sen requested that the defendants be allowed to post bail and be released. Judge Qian reviewed the confessions and ordered that a date be set for sentencing. Gong and Xu each posted 1,500 yuan bail, and Tang posted 1,000 yuan bail to be released pending judgment.

China Children's Year to Begin on April 4th This Year

The Ministry of Education Has Made a Firm Decision

The Grandeur of the American Children's Year

The year 1935 (Republican Year 24) will be China Children's Year. However, because the National Children's Year Preparatory Committee is still being organized within the Ministry of Education, the opening ceremony could not be held on New Year's Day this year. This reporter visited Chen Zhengfan, an executive of the China Child Welfare Association, who stated, "The Ministry of Education has now decided that China Children's Year will begin on April 4th, Children's Day. The Children's Year Preparatory Committee is also actively progressing within the Ministry of Education. The US government held American Children's Year in 1918, with the opening ceremony held on April 6th of that year and concluding on April 5th, 1919. Our country's decision to start on April 4th is quite similar to the situation in the United States at the time and is very appropriate. When the United States held Children's Year, President Wilson was in office. In the Children's Year declaration issued by the United States government, there was a sentence that said, 'For the sake of justice and the nation, we should provide perfect and thorough protection to the patriotic children who currently make up one-third of the national population. To achieve this goal, we are holding Children's Year. We want to save the lives of 100,000 infants and young children nationwide and further develop minimum child welfare standards for health education and labor for all children in the United States.' The American Children's Year movement was led by the Children's Bureau of the United States Department of Labor and promoted by the women's department of the United States National Defense Association. A total of 11 million women participated in the activities, producing 17,000 committees, and there was enthusiastic and active response throughout the country. In addition to the women's sector, countless university professors, church pastors, social workers, and librarians provided assistance in various ways. As a result, first, the infant mortality rate was reduced; second, standards for child rearing in the family were established; third, child labor laws were formulated; fourth, opportunities for outdoor activities, recreation, and entertainment for children were increased; and fifth, the problem of abandonment of orphans and poor children was resolved. It can be said that satisfactory results have been achieved. Our country's Children's Year movement should take the American precedent as a model. The true purpose of holding Children's Year lies in sincerely seeking happiness for children. The success of this effort should be expressed in deeds and in numbers. If the government only issues a decree and holds a few celebration meetings to conclude the event, then where is the meaning of Children's Year? Wouldn't that be completely contrary to the original intention of the initiators? As we prepare to hold Children's Year, I wish to share this sentiment with compatriots across the country. In addition, the Children's Year Song and the Outline of Implementation Methods for Children's Year have been printed and widely distributed nationwide. All child welfare organizations, educational institutions, cultural institutions, religious institutions, social service organizations, etc., in various places can prepare official letters and request them from this association at No. 131 Shanghai Museum Road for reference."

Private Postal Bureau Letter Carrier Detained for Delivering Mail

Waiting for the Postal Bureau Owner to Appear in Court for Further Verification

Private postal bureaus in our country have a long history. Almost every city, town, remote area, and border region has one. Before the establishment of the state-run postal service, private postal bureaus were the only means of communication for merchants. In recent years, the postal service has developed rapidly. The delivery of letters, goods, and remittances has become swift and reliable. The people's faith in the postal service has also become increasingly firm. Last year, the Ministry of Transportation believed that in order to further develop the postal service, private postal bureaus should first be eliminated. Therefore, it issued a circular to the postal administration bureaus of all provinces and cities, instructing them to inform all local private postal bureaus that they must cease operations by the end of the 23rd year of the Republic of China and ordering local administrative offices to assist in suppressing them. Although private postal bureaus everywhere protested and sent representatives to Beijing last month to petition for the continued existence of private postal bureaus in order to maintain the livelihoods of those working in the industry, the transportation authorities believed that the case concerned the development of the national postal service and rejected the request. They further ordered all post offices to refuse the delivery of letters and packages from private postal bureaus starting from New Year's Day this year. However, the private postal bureaus in this city have so far defied the ministry's orders and continue to receive and send letters and operate as usual. The other day, Dong Xiangfa, the owner of the Baoshun Private Postal Bureau at No. 366 Jiujiang Road, still sent letters from various places to Shanghai via the

Unprecedented Heavy Fog Enveloped This City Last Night and This Morning

Shops Operated with Lights On, Vehicles Moved Slowly with Horns Blaring

The Sun Was Dim, Many People Gathered to Watch

Jianghai Ships Were Blocked, Shanghai-Beiping and Shanghai-Hankou Flights Were Delayed

An unprecedented heavy fog occurred in this city yesterday morning, dissipating only at 9:00 AM. When the fog was heavy, people could not be distinguished even at close range. Shops all operated with lights on, and vehicles, even with lights on and horns blaring, moved very slowly and had difficulty driving. As for the ships entering and leaving the port, they were even more affected. At that time, this city had almost completely entered a night scene. A Datong reporter has recorded the various situations obtained below.

A Scene of Night. After dawn yesterday morning, opening the window revealed a misty atmosphere. By 8:30 AM, the fog had become very dense, and people could not be distinguished even at close range. Shops all opened their lights for business, and cars and trams all turned on their lights, rang their bells, or honked their horns and drove slowly. At that time, this city had almost completely entered a night scene.

Dim Sun. The sun rose very early yesterday morning, but it was obscured by heavy fog, its color like solidified grease, its light dim. People gathered on the streets to watch, marveling at the unusual sight. At the same time, a suffocating odor emanated from the fog, which was particularly foul. This heavy fog began to dissipate at 9:05 AM, and the weather became extremely clear and pleasant.

Ships Were Blocked. After the fog cleared, Datong News Agency reporters specifically investigated with the Jianghai Customs and various shipping companies. The ships that were blocked outside the harbor by the fog and only entered the harbor after the fog dissipated included the China Merchants Haiyuan Wheel, Jardine Matheson Hesheng Wheel, Taikoo Qiongzhou Wheel (all from Hong Kong to Shanghai), Haining Wheel (from Saigon to Shanghai), Zhengji Tongli Wheel (from Niuzhuang to Shanghai), Sanbei Ningxing Wheel (from Ningbo to Shanghai), and the Java Mailboat Gas Tokko. Their entry times were all after 9:00 AM, some as late as 1:00 or 2:00 PM. These ships were all supposed to arrive at the port at 5:00 or 6:00 in the morning. As for delayed departures, the Taikoo Huangpu Wheel, which was sailing to the various ports along the Yangtze River, also only left the port at 9:00 AM.

Flights Were Delayed. The China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Hankou flight was also delayed from 7:00 AM to 9:50 AM, a delay of two hours and fifty minutes. The Shanghai-Beiping flight, which was originally scheduled to take off at 6:30 AM, was also delayed until 9:20 AM, a delay of three hours.

When Zhang passed through Ji'an Lane on Henan Road, he was discovered by Lu Youtong, an inspector of the Shanghai Postal Administration Bureau, who believed that Zhang should not be performing a prohibited service. He had him arrested and taken to the police station. Ke Yinghao Claims to Be Japanese and Assaults Lawyer in Court

The Court Must Investigate with the Ministry of Interior

Ke Yinghao, a person from Shang'an Township in Fujian, previously leased No. 5 Ping Le Lane on Xizang Road from Liu Yide's leasing agency. He now owes rent for more than eight months, totaling over 1,600 yuan. The leasing agency hired lawyer Zhu Sifu to file a lawsuit for rent arrears and eviction with the First Special District Local Court. However, when the court bailiff served the summons, Ke suddenly claimed to be Japanese, causing the plaintiff's lawyer, Zhu Sifu, to request the court to order Ke to produce his citizenship certificate as proof at the last hearing. The case was adjourned. Yesterday morning, Judge Luo Chongtai continued the trial in Civil Court 7. Ke Yinghao also appeared in court. The court questioned Ke about his nationality. According to Ke, he is from Shang'an Township in Fujian. In June of the 9th year of the Republic of China (1920), when Qian Nengxun was the prime minister, he became a Japanese citizen. Ji, the Chinese consul in Kobe, Japan, applied to the Chinese Ministry of Interior for his renunciation of Chinese citizenship a year earlier. There is a record of this. He also presented a Japanese citizenship certificate as evidence. Lawyer Zhu Sifu immediately stated that according to Article 11 of the Nationality Law, citizenship cannot be lost without a renunciation certificate from the Ministry of Interior. He requested that the court investigate. At this time, Ke stepped down from the defendant's box and strode around the judge's seat with an arrogant attitude. The court informed him that no matter what nationality people were, they should obey the rules of the court and not act arbitrarily. A court attendant stepped forward to stop him, but Ke refused to obey and went to the lawyer's table and punched lawyer Zhu Sifu, saying, "You said I was impersonating a Japanese citizen. I have to hit you." At the time, his voice was loud and aggressive. The court attendant immediately stepped forward to stop him, and Judge Luo also sternly stopped him. Ke still acted forcefully and said to lawyer Zhu, "When you go outside, I will punch you." At this time, the court ordered the case to be adjourned for further investigation with the Ministry of Interior and adjourned the court. Ke waited for a long time at the court entrance before leaving. Lawyer Zhu waited in the lawyer's lounge for Ke to leave before returning by car, thus avoiding him.

Englishman Wei Bai Commits Suicide

British Consulate Investigating the Cause

Wei Bai, an Englishman, worked in the accounts department of the British American Tobacco Company and resided on the 12th floor of a 13-story building on the corner of Ma'erxi Road on the French Concession. He habitually left in the morning and returned in the evening. Yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM, Wei suddenly told the building's servant that he was feeling unwell and needed to take a nap for an hour, instructing him not to disturb him. After speaking, he tightly closed his door. After about half an hour, a gunshot suddenly rang out from Wei's room. The servant knew something was wrong. When he rushed in to inspect, he saw Wei lying in a pool of blood. Fresh blood was flowing from a bullet hole in his right temple. A lotus-shaped pistol was discarded on the floor. It was clear that he had committed suicide. The building's accounts department reported the incident to the French police station, and the police chief immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. At the same time, the British police station was notified and sent officers to the scene. The British Consulate also heard the news and sent people to the scene to conduct an on-site inspection. The cause of his suicide is currently being investigated in detail by the British Consulate.

Since he was fond of her, he should treat her well and pay him ten thousand dollars to compensate for his loss. After negotiations, Li wrote a four-hundred-yuan promissory note from his friend surnamed Zhu and gave it to Zhou as a hush money.

The matter subsided. The other day at dusk, the Zhu family held a celebratory banquet at the Eastern Hotel on Xizang Road, inviting many guests, including Li and Zhou. At that time, Li Yun's younger brother, Li Yugui, was also at the banquet. To investigate. According to Li Yun, twenty yuan in cash, two gold rings, and a watch had been taken from him by Zhou and the others. Extortion by Intimidation. He requested that they be punished according to the law. Li Yun then testified that he lived at No. 10 Xingjiaqiao Road in Zhabei. After all irrelevant persons had left the court, the court questioned both sides one by one and then concluded the trial. Subsequently, Zhou Peijun was sentenced to a fine of fifty yuan, and Zhou Fang was found not guilty. Changing One Yuan to Three Hundred Yuan

The Adulterer Has Bad Intentions

Shao Rongquan found a Shanghai Bank bankbook in Shao Han's name in the room. Upon closer inspection, the amount of savings was three hundred yuan.
