A Brief History of Ruan Lingyu

Zhang Damin: Past Events Like a Dream, Unbearable to Look Back On

Tang Jishan: A Book of Misunderstandings Leads to Litigation in Court

Ruan Lingyu, a female star who currently holds an important role at the Lianhua Film Company, is a name known to almost everyone, even women and children. She once starred in a certain play, and those familiar with her life story all said that the film was Ms. Ruan's personal account. Ruan was originally from Lingnan. Her father passed away early, and her mother worked as a servant. Ruan was fond of learning. Despite the poverty of her family and the struggle to secure food, she still managed to attend school. In 1927, while studying at Chongde Girls' School, she met Zhang Damin, a native of Zhongshan County. Zhang was from a wealthy family and was only twenty-four or twenty-five years old at the time and not yet married, while Ruan was only nineteen. Due to the disparity in their wealth, they could not immediately become a couple. Later, when Ruan's mother was dismissed by her employer, Zhang, feeling that the mother and daughter were in increasingly dire straits, provided financial assistance. Ruan then vowed to devote herself to him for life. Just as the agreement was made, Zhang's mother passed away, making it difficult to hold the wedding immediately. Ruan, fearing that things would change over time, took the opportunity to move into Zhang's house and observe mourning together. From then on, they were practically husband and wife. Later, Zhang went to Hong Kong, serving as a comprador for the Ruian Steamboat and as the director of the Fuqing County Tax Office in Fujian Province, among other positions. He always left Ruan in Shanghai. However, when Zhang was working in Fujian Province, Tang Jishan, a fellow townsman of Zhang's who is now the manager of the Huacha Company, often visited Zhang's house. Over time, he became acquainted with Ruan. They often went to dance halls and theaters together, which eventually led to a romantic relationship. Ruan had never formally married Zhang, and her status was not proper. After becoming involved with Tang, she took the opportunity to take her clothes and belongings, along with her daughter Zhang Miaorong, and left Zhang's house to officially follow Tang. Recently, Zhang Damin has taken a job at the Yida Industrial Company on Sichuan Road in Shanghai. Suddenly, the old matter was brought up again, and he consulted with lawyer Sun Biwu, intending to take legal action against Ruan and Tang. On the 27th of last month, lawyer Sun, acting on behalf of Zhang Damin, sent a letter to Tang Jishan, accusing him of stealing property and misappropriating clothing worth over three thousand yuan, and of privately forging Zhang's seal. After receiving the letter, Tang believed that all the accusations were untrue and immediately hired lawyer Xiong Fei to sue Zhang Damin in the First Special District District Court for fabricating facts and defaming his reputation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Yingchao opened the court to hear the case. After the plaintiff presented his case, the defendant Zhang Damin also detailed his seven or eight years of cohabitation with Ruan Lingyu, and how Tang Jishan took advantage of his absence to visit his home, leading to an affair with Ruan. Ruan then took her clothes and belongings, left his family, and remarried Tang Jishan. He also stated that after returning to Shanghai, he had discussed the matter with lawyer Sun Biwu, intending to entrust lawyer Sun to file a lawsuit, but he had not instructed Sun to send a letter to Tang. Subsequently, lawyer Hong Shihao defended the defendant, arguing that the elements of the crime of defamation, according to Article 325 of the Criminal Law, require an intention to disseminate to the public and to point out or relate facts sufficient to damage another person's reputation. In this case, only one letter from lawyer Sun exists. It is questionable whether this constitutes the crime. Moreover, the letter is not even the defendant's assertion. The court should investigate this carefully. After both sides finished their arguments, the court announced that it would announce the verdict next Thursday afternoon.

Announcement of the Rules of the Jianghai Customs Tariff Review Council

Merchants who have objections to fines or confiscation

May state the reasons and submit them to the Customs within ten days for cancellation

The Jianghai Customs Tariff Review Council has been established, and its various rules and regulations are now ordered to be copied and announced. The original text of the rules is as follows:

Procedure for Request (1) Merchants may apply to the Customs for blank requests and fill them out in Chinese according to the form. If the columns in the request are insufficient, they may be filled in on another sheet. (2) If a merchant receives a written notice of a case handled by the Customs Tax Office and has any objections, he shall submit three copies of the request within ten days for the Customs to handle. (3) If the Customs Tax Office considers it inappropriate to approve the request, it shall submit two copies of the original request to the General Customs Office for decision within ten days, and fill in the details of the case and the reasons in the Tax Office's opinion column of the request. (4) After the request is decided by the Customs Administration, three copies of the decision shall be issued to the General Customs Office, one copy shall be kept, and the remaining two copies shall be sent to the original Customs for filing and forwarded to the original merchant.

Rules of the Review Council Article 1 This Council is organized by the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance in accordance with the provisions of Article 31 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations. Article 2 The members of this Council shall be appointed by the Director of the Customs Administration from among the staff of the Administration, and two shall be appointed from among the staff of the General Customs Office. Article 3 If a Customs Tax Office considers that a merchant's request to cancel a fine or confiscation is unjustified, it shall state the reasons and submit them together with the original request to the General Customs Office for review by the Customs Administration within ten days of receiving the request. Article 4 If the Council does not need to investigate the cases submitted by the Customs Administration, it shall hold a meeting for review within ten days. The presence of four members of the Council shall constitute a quorum. Article 5 The results of the Council's review shall take effect after being decided by the Customs Administration. Article 6 These Rules shall come into effect on the date of promulgation.

Huasheng Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Factory in this city is the first electrical appliance manufacturing factory in China. It has been established for 20 years. High Schools in This City Will Implement Centralized Military Training This Summer

The entire plan has been finalized and submitted to the Ministry for approval.

Participating schools are preparing to make up the courses in advance.

High school military training students in various provinces and cities will implement centralized training starting this summer. In this city, the National Military Training Committee is responsible for the preparation. The Shanghai News reporter asked Jiao Jihua, the chairman of the committee, about the preparation situation and the recent work of the committee as follows.

Centralized Military Training Will Be Implemented This Summer

The centralized military training in this city is scheduled to start in April and end in July this summer, for a total of three months. All high school and equivalent school military training students in this city will participate, totaling more than 4,700 people. A total team system will be adopted, with brigades, battalions, companies, and squads. The location problem, which was once rumored to borrow the Shanghai Racecourse, is not true. It is currently being sought and has not yet been determined. All the implementation plans for centralized military training have been drafted and reported to the Training Headquarters for approval. All schools participating in centralized military training are preparing to make up the courses during the winter vacation. As for junior colleges and above, they will still follow the original method and implement summer military training this year.

Live Firing Will Start in the Next Semester

This semester, schools have begun shooting training. The procedure is divided into three steps: blank firing, reduced-load firing, and live firing. Blank firing has been completed, and reduced-load firing is currently being started. All are held separately by the schools. Live firing will start training from the next semester. The location is in the West Fort.

In order to connect with the military instructors of various schools and discuss military training issues, the committee held a dinner for the military instructors of various schools at the YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge the other day. More than 50 military instructors from various schools attended. During the meeting, Director Jiao of the Military Training Committee reported on the work of the committee and future plans. Then, they exchanged opinions on military training education issues and dispersed.

Regularly Scheduled Principal Meetings

To promote military education in all schools and to facilitate communication between principals and instructors, the association held a principal meeting this semester. As the semester is coming to an end, a second principal meeting will be convened within days to discuss all ongoing matters. Furthermore, all schools should uniformly follow the standards set by the association when purchasing military training equipment.

The Chinese Arts and Crafts Society to Hold its First Board Meeting after Reorganization Tomorrow

Board Members to be Inaugurated Concurrently

Future Society Affairs to be Discussed

The Chinese Arts and Crafts Society has been established for nearly twenty years. In the past, the society's internal organization was divided into a general affairs department and an editorial department under the board of directors. Recently, with the development of the society's affairs, the original organization was no longer sufficient to cope with the situation. Therefore, the society's constitution was amended last year, and the organization was changed. Eleven directors were elected to form a board of directors, responsible for supervising the progress of the society's affairs. The general affairs and editorial departments were merged into a general office, with a director-general and several officers stationed at the society to preside over all matters. The number of members of the board of directors was increased to attract talent. The election of the first board of directors was held on December 16th of last month, and the elected members are Fu Shishuo, Ma Zongrong, Zhou Changshou, Pan Gongzhan, He Bingsong, Bai Pengfei, Zheng Zhenwen, Chen Lifu, Liu Baimin, Tan Qinyu, and Zhou Xianwen. The board of directors has now scheduled its first meeting for tomorrow (the 12th) at 5 p.m. at the society, at which the board members will be inaugurated and the society's policy will be discussed.

Wang Xinmin, He Bingsong, and Others Publish a Declaration on Chinese-Centric Cultural Construction

(Part Two)

Around 1915 and 1916, China was mired in revolutionary setbacks, internal crises, and foreign aggression. Many people believed that politics was not enough to save the country and that cultural means were needed. Thus, the May Fourth Cultural Movement, centered on liberating thought and breaking fetters, arose. Through this movement, the thinking of the Chinese people underwent a transformation.

The new awakening demanded new activities. The Chinese Revolutionary Party, which had led the Xinhai Revolution, was reorganized in response to the times, and political movements unfolded on a large scale. The cry to overthrow warlords and imperialism spread throughout the country, forming a great National Revolution. Despite various twists and turns, China's political transformation finally achieved considerable success after several years of effort.

The current problem at this time is national construction. Construction in the political and economic fields has already begun, and cultural construction should also be started, and it is even more urgent. However, how to construct Chinese culture is a question that urgently needs to be discussed. Some people think that China should return to the past, but ancient China has become history. History cannot be repeated, nor does it need to be repeated. Some people think that China should completely imitate the United Kingdom and the United States. The United Kingdom and the United States have their own characteristics, but China, which is not the United Kingdom or the United States, should have its own unique ideology. Moreover, China is now in a period of transition between an agricultural feudal society and an industrial society, which is different from the United Kingdom and the United States, which have completely entered the industrial era. Therefore, we cannot agree to completely imitate the United Kingdom and the United States. In addition to those who advocate imitating the United Kingdom and the United States, there are two other factions, one advocating imitating Soviet Russia and the other advocating imitating Italy and Germany. However, their errors are exactly the same as those who advocate imitating the United Kingdom and the United States, which is to underestimate the particularity of China's space and time.

Currently, various different views are competing with each other, and China has become a battlefield for various different views. Moreover, the demonic hands of various international cultural aggressions, which penetrate various different views, are also secretly active, each wanting to win the final victory. Can we let them fight in chaos?

Three, what should we do? No, we cannot let it develop naturally. We demand a Chinese-centric cultural construction. In the process of construction, we should have the following understanding: One, China is China, not any region, and therefore has its own particularity. At the same time, China is the China of today, not the China of the past, and has its own certain temporality. Therefore, we pay special attention to the needs of this time and this place. The needs of this time and this place are the basis of the Chinese standard. Two, it is useless to simply praise ancient Chinese systems and ideas, and it is equally useless to simply curse ancient Chinese systems and ideas. It is necessary to examine everything in the past, keep what should be kept, and remove what should be removed. The commendable good systems and great ideas should be vigorously promoted and contributed to the world, while the condemnable bad systems and inferior ideas should be eliminated as much as possible, without any reluctance. Three, it is necessary and appropriate to absorb European and American culture, but we must absorb what should be absorbed, and we should not absorb even the dregs with an attitude of complete acceptance. The standard of absorption should be determined by the needs of modern China. Four, Chinese wooden cultural construction is creation, a creation that catches up with the head. The purpose of creation is to enable China and the Chinese people, who have declined in the cultural field due to the loss of characteristics, to not only be able to keep pace with other countries and people in the cultural field, but also to make the most valuable contribution to the world's culture. Five, we are building China in culture, not abandoning the ideal of universal harmony, but building China first, becoming a whole and healthy unit, and having sufficient power to promote world harmony. In short, China must have a self-awareness, but also a world vision, both the generosity of not closing itself off, and the determination not to blindly imitate. This understanding can be considered a profound understanding.

Moving forward along this understanding, our cultural construction should be: not conservative, not blindly following, based on the Chinese standard, adopting a critical attitude, and applying scientific methods to examine the past, grasp the present, and create the future. Not conservative means eliminating the old culture, removing its dregs, keeping its essence, and striving to open up new roads. Not blindly following means taking the good points and abandoning the bad, choosing the good and following it, and still not losing self-awareness in following the good. Based on the Chinese standard, adopt a critical attitude, and apply scientific methods to examine the past, grasp the present, and create the future, which is to settle the past mistakes, supply the current needs, and determine the future direction, and use cultural means to produce a bright and warm China, so that China can restore its past glory in the cultural field, reoccupy an important position, and become the strongest and most powerful force in promoting world harmony. (End)

Yan Youzhi to Study in the UK

Ms. Yan Youzhi graduated from the Second Jiangsu Provincial Normal School in 1922. After that, she continued to study mathematics and physics at Datong University and was a proud student of Mr. Wu Zaiyuan. She has served as a mathematics and physics teacher at Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai High School, Jinan University Affiliated High School, Faculty of Law, Southeast Medical College, and other schools. She is enthusiastic in her guidance and highly respected by her colleagues. She is also trusted by her students.

In addition to teaching, she also compiled and translated mathematics and physics textbooks, which are popular throughout the country. In recent years, she also founded the Longmen Printing Bureau, which is also popular throughout the country, and edited and printed various scientific books, making great contributions to schools and academic circles. Now, Ms. Yan still feels that her academic knowledge is insufficient and has decided to go to the UK to study applied chemistry at the University of Glasgow, paying particular attention to printing, photography, pigments, and other subjects. It is said that she is scheduled to sail on the Conte Rosso on the 15th of this month. It is expected that after returning to China, she will definitely make greater contributions to the academic and industrial circles in the country.

New Year's Day Hong Kong Holds Guangdong-Hong Kong Track and Field Competition

Champion: Guangdong Guangnan Team 96 points

Runner-up: Hong Kong British Navy 37 points

Third Place: Hong Kong South China Team 34 points

(Hong Kong Correspondence) The Guangdong track and field team competition had been in the works for a long time and had not yet been held. It was not until New Year's Day this year that it was finally realized in Hong Kong. First, the Guangdong Guangnan track and field team and the Hong Kong South China Athletic Association completed the negotiation of the arrangements. On the 31st of the previous month, dozens of members of the Guangnan team set off from Guangzhou. The leaders were Guo Songtang, Zhao Shanxing, and Qiu Jixiang; the coach was Zhang Weixin; the captains were Zhong Lianji and Zhao Hui; the Chinese secretary was Chen Futian; the Western secretary was Wang Minxian; and the staff were Zhao Bingheng, Cao Zhaohui, and He Yunsong. The team members included (sprint) Zhao Bingheng, Zhu Zhongxi, He Peigen, Fu Jiagui; (middle distance) Zhao Hui, Chen Futian, Han Yingguang, Lin Kai; (hurdles) Zhong Lianji, Li Jinquan, Chen Yaosheng; (jumps) Cao Zhaohui, Wang Minxian, Chen Yaochi, Ma Deguang, Zhang Qijun; (throws) Liang Zhichu, Guo Zemin, Huang Tianan, Jin Zizhang, Zhang Xuetong; women's team: Situ Wei (manager), members Zhao Yunshan, Li Yuanfen, Liang Qianhua, Zhang Jieqiong, Yan Xiurong, Kuang Yuzhen, Xue Dong, Li Yulan, He Jingxiong, Zhong Jinping. After arriving in Hong Kong, they were hosted by the Hong Kong South China Association, and the Hong Kong British Navy track and field team was also invited to participate, forming a triangular competition. On New Year's Day, despite the heavy rain, the competition was held at 2:00 pm at the South China Sports Field on Caroline Hill in Hong Kong. During the competition, the rain did not stop, and the slippery track greatly affected the results. As a result, the Guangdong Guangnan team won first place with 96 points, the Hong Kong British Navy team came in second with 37 points, and the Hong Kong South China team came in third with 34 points. After the competition, the Hong Kong South China Association held a welcome party and presented the championship prizes. The captain of the Guangdong Guangnan team then gave a reply and presented commemorative flags to the Hong Kong South China Association and the Hong Kong British Navy. The atmosphere was very enthusiastic. This time, the Guangnan women's team did not have an opponent in Hong Kong, so the competition was not held. It is learned that the Guangnan team returned to the province on the 3rd. The results of this Guangdong-Hong Kong inter-city track and field competition are listed below:

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seven: Hearing Words, Covering Tearful Traces, Selling Oneself to Tell Hardships, Discreetly Seeking Eastern Reliance with Ardent Affection

Only then did Yueying force out a word, wiping away tears, and said, "Thank you, Mr. Cheng." As she spoke, she stood up. At this moment, Wang Beihai, who had been sitting in the corner, suddenly stood up and waved his hand, saying, "Hold on, I have something to say." Everyone was taken aback; what could he have to say at this time? He waited for Yueying to stop, but did not speak to Yueying. He turned to Aunt Hu and said, "I heard Mr. Cheng's words and feel very sorry for you. However, my strength is limited, and I cannot help you much. I brought six or seven catties of sorghum cakes from home, and I can share half of them with you." As he spoke, he untied the bundle on the table, revealing more than twenty large sorghum cakes inside. Cheng Zhishu smiled and waved his hand at him, saying, "Saving people is indeed a duty of mankind, but saving people in a well only results in falling into the well yourself. I don't approve of this. It's good that you have this intention, but there's no need to give it to them. Otherwise, where will you find half a week's worth of food?" As he spoke, he smiled at Li Shilian, saying, "Mr. Li won't understand this unless I explain it clearly. The students in Xi'an are very hardworking. Look at the set of clothes he's wearing; it's almost like this all year round. Students in Shanghai and Beiping probably sleep on iron beds as a matter of course, but they all sleep on earthen pits. Especially when it comes to food, you wouldn't believe it." As he spoke, he pointed to the dark sorghum cakes on the table and said, "This stuff is from the countryside, not from the city of Chang'an. If the student's home is no more than thirty or fifty miles from the city, they will walk home on Saturday afternoon and return to the city on Sunday afternoon. This trip is not for anything else but to go back and get this stuff. Sorghum cakes are worthless, but how these sorghum cakes are brought to Chang'an is worth studying. Because of this, I don't approve of Wang Jun giving sorghum cakes to Aunt Hu. Besides, he only has seven catties of sorghum cakes each week, which is barely enough to eat. If he gives half of it away, where will he get the other half?" (109)

Sacred Drama

— Qing Qu

In the midst of rural bankruptcy, is it not a contradictory and strange thing to suddenly hear the words "sacred drama"? Last week, in the northwest of Jiading, in a place called "Laozhu Hui," a grand sacred drama was staged. It is said that the cost of this performance was raised by using the name of the Bodhisattva in the temple to solicit donations from house to house. Moreover, this time, the Jianghu opera troupe, named Tianji Grand Stage, had complete roles and decent costumes, so it attracted an especially large number of spectators from all over the villages. However, after four plays were performed, the surrounding fields, like beans and wheat, were undoubtedly trampled on a lot. But a group of villagers still said that performing the drama for a few days this year to honor the Bodhisattva would surely bring a year of abundance and a full harvest! What kind of talk is this!

Oh! Don't blame the countryside; it's not that the farmers have no knowledge and want to stage sacred dramas. Even now, people in the city are very happy to watch dramas. They have to borrow the authority of the Fire God Bodhisattva. As long as there is a leading qualification, they immediately take out the yellow book of names and say a few words of reverence to the gods, and money will naturally be taken out. And there are dramas to watch, so who wouldn't be willing? As a result, a small Fire God Temple became so noisy that the walls almost collapsed and people were crushed to death. Also, because the opera troupe's expenses were not enough, in addition to honoring the gods, they moved to the Yimiao Temple at night to sell tickets. Although the venue was slightly larger, it was still packed. Especially the viewing stands were arranged without any gaps, but there were too many spectators, and there were constant sounds of the stands collapsing. There were even people who had their feet crushed and injured. Can you imagine how pitiful that is!

The most ridiculous thing is that people who save money and don't sit in the stands stand in the square, called "Zha Tai Qian" (squeezing in front of the stage). These people are very strong. Although they sometimes resemble a tide, they can still struggle to stand on their feet. Those who are not strong will be squeezed down, and even lose their footing, and their shoes will fall off. They pick them up and throw them onto the stage, piling them up high. Therefore, when the play ends, people often leave barefoot, stepping on the ground with socks, indicating that they have come back from watching the play. Or they have to go to the shoe store and buy new ones to put on before leaving. Alas! Don't laugh at the farmers in the countryside; in fact, the people in the city watching plays at the theater are just like them. What's the grandfather laughing at the grandmother for!

Snippets

— (Tu Hongxia)

Jin Shengtan of the Romance of the Three Kingdoms said: "The eighteen lords could not kill Dong Zhuo, but Diao Chan was enough to kill him; Liu, Guan, and Zhang could not defeat Lu Bu, but Diao Chan, a woman, could defeat him; she used the bed as a battlefield, rouge and powder as armor, glances as spears, smiles as bows and arrows, sweet words and flattery as strategic deployment, a female general is truly to be feared!" Since ancient times, beauties have suppressed heroes, and heroes have succumbed to beauties. Is this only a modern phenomenon?

Iron Dumbbells

— Hu Chenzhou

During my school days, I never loved the subject of "physical education." As soon as I left school, life oppressed me, and I spent my days hunched over between ink bottles and pens, without even a chance to stretch my arms or kick my legs. As a result, I became thinner and weaker. Whenever I encountered someone with a chest out and belly protruding, I couldn't help but shudder, and my head would naturally bow down in front of them.

I was only twenty years old, but I was already so weak; this simply didn't make sense. In today's society, where individualism has reached its peak, conflicts between people are inevitable. The weak will be pressed under the buttocks of the strong and used as a stool, unable to even hum a low sound! Moreover, justice is built on the foundation of iron and blood! If others aggressively come at you with weapons, you cannot possibly meet them with a pen and say, "Come, let me reason with you!"

There are quite a few tools for practicing "martial arts": the "eighteen weapons," the immortal's burden, stone locks... like those heroes we often see showing off on the streets. There are also foreign boxing coaches' Chest Expanders, sandbags, etc., but I always felt that those were not convenient to practice with and were easy to get injured with. I unintentionally heard someone mention iron dumbbells. I had done dumbbell exercises in school before, although those were wooden; now I would just add a little weight.

Finally, I bought a pair of iron dumbbells, each weighing twelve pounds. Every day, early in the morning, before the sun had even risen, I left the bed, regardless of how low the temperature of my humble abode was due to the influence of winter. I put on a set of shorts and opened all the windows and doors! The northwest wind completed its exchange effect in my humble abode. In front was the web ball field: readily available fresh air! (I should thank its master, the gentleman in the big house over there!) From my hazy memory, I picked out the dumbbell exercises, so fragmented, so incomplete... "Up, down, left, right, forward, backward!"

At first, I felt that the two black things were awfully heavy. After doing a few reps, my arms immediately started to ache and I couldn't support them. Now my arms are getting thicker every day! The bodies of those iron dumbbells are already engraved with many white scars.

Fighting a Path to Survival

Imperial Fragrance Misty Record

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

In order to show that he truly had such qualifications, he had to use hunting as a kind of proof. Therefore, when he saw even the fiercest tigers or leopards, he could not show the slightest fear, otherwise those who accompanied him on the hunt would inevitably laugh at him in private. This was only a test of his courage and was not enough to show his skill in archery and horsemanship. To test his archery and horsemanship, weasels were the most suitable test, because although weasels are very small, their leg strength is extremely strong, and they run faster than anything else. Moreover, their bodies are very agile, and unless someone is proficient in archery, it is impossible to shoot them. If an emperor could often hunt weasels, his reputation for good shooting would surely be praised by the whole country! As for the use of the sword, it was different. Usually, it was prepared but not used. Only those leaders who were truly courageous and extremely skilled in martial arts, in order to make their people sincerely fear them, would deliberately abandon bows and arrows and specially ride their horses over to fight a tiger or a leopard within five steps, showing off their swordsmanship to the fullest. However, this kind of situation was very rare!"

The Empress Dowager's above remarks only explained to us the general situation of emperors' hunting and the reasons why they often hunted. As for what constituted a detailed program for completing a hunt, she had not yet mentioned it. We couldn't help but feel very anxious, so she got to the main point. (219)

Rebuilding the Tomb of Mr. Zhou Lianxi

— (Guan Wu)

The Song Confucian scholar Zhou Dunyi, courtesy name Maoshu, came from a family in Lianxi Township, Yingdao County, Dao Prefecture. He wrote dozens of works such as "Explanation of the Taiji Diagram" and "Tong Shu," integrating metaphysics and physics, unifying them into one. The two gentlemen of Yichuan and Mingdao were both his disciples, and he was truly the ancestor of Daoist learning. Mr. Zhou was born in the first year of Tianxi during the reign of Emperor Zhenzong of the Song Dynasty and died in the sixth year of Xining during the reign of Emperor Shenzong, at the age of fifty-seven. He was buried at the foot of Lianfeng Mountain in Mount Lu, Jiangxi. His tomb had been in disrepair for many years. Bao County Magistrate of Jiujiang, Mr. Ren, in order to promote the sages and preserve historical sites, initiated the restoration. Although there were proponents and sponsors, there was no final decision. It is said that this time, the Red Swastika Society's relief team went to Jiangxi for relief. It happened that the team leader was Zhou Zongliang, a descendant of Mr. Zhou Lianxi. County Magistrate Bao occasionally talked about it with him, and he was extremely moved. Mr. Zhou generously agreed to be solely responsible for the restoration, estimated at 4,000 yuan. County Magistrate Bao has already planned specific measures and will start construction soon, and plans to build a road in front of the tomb to connect to the highway. From now on, Jiujiang will have one more scenic spot, which is also a good story.

Where Travels Lead

Shanghai-Guangdong Sightseeing Trip Encounters Fog

— Qian Hua

The China National Aviation Corporation recently purchased two of the latest Douglas seaplanes from the United States, each worth US$60,000, equivalent to about 200,000 yuan in national currency, named Guangdong and Fujian respectively, specializing in flying the Shanghai-Guangdong line, ensuring passenger safety. It was originally scheduled to test the new aircraft on January 1st of this year and invite the Chinese and Western press in this city to ride along and sightseeing. Unexpectedly, due to bad weather, it was postponed to the 3rd. On the 3rd, the weather was still not good, so it was postponed to 7:00 am on the 6th before the trip finally took place. That morning, at six o'clock, in the dim morning light, I took a car to Longhua Airport. I arrived at the airport at 6:30, and many people were already waiting in the passenger room. Mr. He Zhijing, Deputy Director of the company's business department, personally greeted us and introduced us to Mr. Dai Enji, the general manager of the company. Mr. Dai then introduced the other reporters traveling with us: Mr. Wang Jiao of the Shenshi Telegraph Agency, Ms. Luo Qian of the North-China Daily News, Mr. Paul Mendon of The Times, and Mr. Gold of the China Press, along with Mr. Dai and me, a total of six people. Then, the passengers and luggage were weighed one by one and recorded on an aircraft load sheet. Finally, pilot Fangs carefully read the load sheet and said "OK," and we began to depart. The staff in the company hurriedly handed out small paper packets to each person, containing a piece of Red Cross cotton wool and a packet of Wrigley's Spearmint gum. The cotton wool was for plugging the ears to prevent excessive vibration from the engine noise and could be tried.

The seaplane was parked on the water. We boarded the Fujian aircraft from the pier one after another. The passenger seats were arranged in rows of three, on the left and right sides. Miss Luo Qian went first and sat with Mr. Gold in the first row, Paul Mendon and Mr. Dai sat in the second row, and Mr. Wang and I sat in the back. At exactly 7:00, the pilot started the engine, and the plane slowly taxied on the water, going faster and faster, and the waves became higher and higher. Finally, the glass windows on both sides of the passengers were almost submerged in the water. At that instant, the plane lifted off the water and soared straight up. Looking down at the Huangpu River and the houses near Longhua, everything was clearly visible, and my heart was filled with joy.

In our small group, the American pilot, Fangs, seemed to be the commander-in-chief, wielding the power of life and death over the entire aircraft. The radio operator, Mr. Chen, next to him, seemed to be the head of the intelligence department, constantly communicating news with the outside world and reporting internally. Mr. Dai seemed like a university professor, constantly explaining the places we passed and the news from outside. And our group of reporters were just like students in a lecture hall, quickly taking notes of the professor's lectures. This is Hangzhou Bay, this is the coastline, these are the Zhoushan Islands, this is Zhongxiang Island, this is Zhenhai at the entrance to Ningbo. We spread out the map for reference, and the scenery below the window was our very concrete experimental field.

Mr. Gold was the most talkative, and his words were humorous, filling the cabin with laughter. Mr. Wang and I were old classmates from Yenching University, and we enjoyed chatting about past events even more. Mr. Dai busied himself with arrangements, taking out a few wool blankets from the luggage area in the back and asking us to cover our lower bodies. Originally, my legs and feet felt a little cold, but with the blankets, it was truly wonderful. Mr. Dai also took out Sullivan's sandwich bread, and we devoured it, truly warm and full. Sitting inside the plane, we didn't feel how fast we were going. After an hour, the pilot reported that we had already traveled 155 miles, equivalent to 465 li, which was truly unexpected. (To be continued)

Broach 144.75 5.00 37.40

Furthermore, according to a Bombay dispatch, the opening forecast for Broach cotton on the 10th was 242 biro, down 2 rupees 7.5 cents from the previous day's close.

According to a report from the Sin Fung Foreign Firm, the cotton deadlock has not yet been resolved. Farmers and the government are still not releasing cotton. Meanwhile, preparations for the next planting season are underway. Those who are impatient with long positions are gradually liquidating. The ambiguity in legislation before the Supreme Court's ruling and the lack of production quotas in the Peng Kehai case make it difficult to expand the scope of transactions. It is reported that there have been large transactions in fertilizers and agricultural implements.

Trend of Hedging Sales of Grain Futures and Flour Gradually Subsides

Yesterday in the flour market, after the opening in the morning, the market for each month showed a pattern of first weakening and then stabilizing. The quoted prices for foreign wheat were around 12.3 cents lower for Chicago wheat and 8 cents to 16 cents lower for Canadian wheat. At the opening, the quotes for foreign wheat were lower, and the previous day's order of one ship of foreign wheat further weakened sentiment for all months, down by one to one and a half cents from the previous day. However, there were few factory hedges, and the customer support was not weak, so the decline was limited. By the afternoon opening, since factories were not issuing and hedgers were also taking a wait-and-see approach, trading was light and the market stabilized. As the settlement date for the Lunar New Year approached, customer trading mostly stopped, leading to a consolidation pattern in the later stages. As a result, the current month was unchanged, February was down slightly by 0.25 cents, March was down slightly by 0.75 cents, April was down slightly by 0.25 cents, May was down slightly by 0.25 cents, and June was down slightly by 0.05 cents.

Stagnation and Weakness in Wheat Futures

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was generally quiet after the opening in the morning. The quoted prices for foreign wheat were down by 8 cents to 12.3 cents. At the opening, the market for each month was stagnant, and trading was light, with prices down by 2 to 3 cents from the previous day. By the afternoon opening, the market remained weak due to some foreign wheat hedging, which dampened sentiment. The smaller moves in the distant months were due to this. As a result, the current month was down 0.3 cents, February was down 0.5 cents, March was down 0.4 cents, and April was down 0.5 cents. In the spot wheat market, the standard grade was weak, with secondary grades down 1-2 cents. Shandong Suzhou Guide wheat was quoted at 4.034 yuan, Yaowan wheat at 3.956 yuan, and Liuhe wheat at 4.01 yuan, secondary at 0.98 yuan, totaling 5,000 bags, which were reportedly handled by Fuxin.

Chicago wheat spot prices are stable. Purchases by factories and the Far East, the impending shipment of wheat from Argentina and Australia, and the ample reserves of Canadian wheat will all affect future prices. The United States does not lack wheat, but will only reduce the surplus.

Speculators Emerge in Rice Futures Market

Nervous Sentiment...Continued Weakness Across All Boards

Yesterday, the rice market was even weaker. A ship of newly arrived Iraeli Tapi Simara rice arrived (this was loaded in November and is the last ship for November; there are still two ships for December that have not arrived and are expected to arrive in Shanghai soon). The market has ample reserves and new arrivals are continuous. Although sales are active, sentiment is very nervous. Yesterday, over 4,000 bags of spot rice were offered, and prices continued to fall by 0.05 to 0.1 yuan. Sellers in the rice futures market continued to seek buyers, while speculators are nervous and eager to sell. Buyers are taking a wait-and-see approach. Only 300 tons of Mindon Saigon rice for April were offered at 4.85 yuan, but there were 2-3,000 tons transacted in the gray market at lower prices than the market offers. This further panicked customer speculators seeking to sell. However, new transactions have stopped yesterday. If the floating inventory in the market is cleared, the market may stabilize again. The arrival and inventory of customer Indica rice are both low, and merchants are still not willing to sell off completely. Over 2,000 bags were offered yesterday, and spot prices were affected by the rice market, also falling by 0.05 to 0.06 yuan.

Sunny Weather Causes Downriver Rice to Drop Again by 0.2 to 0.3 Yuan

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, over thirty sources from various regions arrived (totaling nearly 6,000 shi). The market situation has carried over from the previous day's decline, and coupled with the clear weather, sentiment has softened further, resulting in sluggish sales. Prices have steadily decreased, falling by about 0.3 yuan. Prices for various late Indica rice and thick japonica rice have all depreciated by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. Looking at the overall situation, there is a sense of listlessness, and there is concern that the market may weaken further. Tuyang Jian rice is in relatively good shape due to a shortage of goods in recent days, but the Yinbian rice price still followed the Japonica market and fell by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, over forty sources from various regions downriver arrived. In terms of sales, white japonica rice and various pointed early thin rice were sluggish. Only Yinbian rice was slightly transacted, with total sales estimated at over 1,000 shi. In terms of market prices, high-quality white japonica rice was down by a small number of cents, medium-quality rice was unchanged, Yinbian rice was down by 0.1 yuan, Yangjian rice was down by a few cents, thin rice was down by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan, and the remaining goods were generally weak.

Soybean Sales Turn Sluggish

Yesterday, the soybean market declined by 0.04 to 0.05 yuan due to the fact that although the Anhui donation to the provincial government could not be avoided, the higher authorities had dispatched supervisors to abolish it within a limited time, which caused some nervous sentiment and led to an initial drop. In addition, sales in various regions have been sluggish in the past two days. Valuing a large amount of Yangtze River soybeans, and under the circumstances of tight credit, the market turned down due to various reasons. Yesterday, 1,500 bags of Hankou Zha soybeans were transacted, with prices ranging from 3.63 yuan to 3.65 yuan. 200 bags of Hankou late soybeans were transacted at 3.42 yuan. Two cars of Dalian Siping Street soybeans were quoted at 4.05 yuan. One car of Yingzhou aged soybeans was quoted at 3.8 yuan, and 500 bags of Guide soybeans were quoted at 3.75 yuan.

Sugar Market: Coarse Sand and White Sugar Rise by 0.1 Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market trend remained tight. The guild's price fixing for #24 coarse sand white ordinary spot sugar, which had been quoted at 18.95 yuan the day before but not transacted, was fixed at 19 yuan yesterday. Transshipment goods were at 5.4 yuan, up 0.1 yuan from before. #8-9 Dutch red sugar spot goods were at 13.9 yuan, and transshipment goods in bonded warehouses were at 4.8 yuan. Taikoo sugar B mark was at 19.3 yuan, and the factory's refined white sugar #1 was at 18.2 yuan. Due to a shortage of goods, Chao traders offered over 1,000 bags of newly arrived Chaoqing, with Tizhuangqing at 11 yuan, Huanggangqing at 10.6 to 10.4 yuan, Bannanqing at 10.23 yuan, and Longgangqing at 10 to 9.9 yuan, up 0.2 yuan from before. Guangdong traders offered dozens of baskets of Changan Pianqing at 9.8 yuan, and Jian traders offered hundreds of pieces of Quanzhouqing at 9.7 yuan.

Dried Longan from Shima is Short Due to Scarcity

The dried longan market in Shima has recently seen rising land prices and a limited supply of goods. It is reported that the branded goods have already been cleared, and merchants' inventory is also limited. Therefore, there is a significant shortage now. It has been found that the market price for ordinary branded goods has reached 54 yuan. If goods with bright red color, good quality, dryness, and large size arrive, prices can be further increased. It is expected that a small number of shipments will be delivered later to meet sales needs.

Hardware: Tinplate Prices Rise by Over 1 Yuan

The tinplate market has been quite good recently. Although transactions have not increased due to the end of the year, quoted prices are brisk and the supply of new arrivals is scarce. Therefore, the market is exceptionally firm. Current market quotes are as follows (unit: yuan):

90 lbs American 16.25 180 lbs American 33.00

90 lbs German 16.00 180 lbs German 32.75

90 lbs French 15.75 180 lbs French 32.50

100 lbs American 17.00 200 lbs American 35.00

100 lbs German 16.50 200 lbs German 34.00

100 lbs French 16.50 200 lbs French 33.50

Compared to the previous day, single-linked goods are up 0.5 to 0.6 yuan, and double-linked goods are up 1.1 to 1.2 yuan. Aside from sporadic openings by retail stores, there have been no reports of large transactions. According to industry insiders, overseas quoted prices are rising daily, and credit in the local market is very tight. If those holding goods can hold on for one or two weeks, then this market will definitely open up. It is found that only 200-300 boxes were transacted in the market yesterday.

Silk and Tea: Zhenmei Green Tea from Wuyuan Shows Slight Movement in European Sales

The sales of Zhenmei green tea from the northern route of Wuyuan have been sluggish. Yesterday, Jinlong Shuixing and other firms received telegrams from Africa requesting purchases. 170 boxes have already been purchased. Sprout tea is quoted at 110 yuan, and ordinary tea is sold for 70 to 73 yuan, which is 3-4 yuan lower than at the end of last year. Needle tea and Xiumei green tea were also purchased by British firms such as Yingzhuang Xiehe and Dude in the market yesterday. However, sales prices still declined because Chinese merchants are eager to sell off.

Oil Market: Newly Produced Raw Oil Scarce in Wuhan Market

Since the price surge in raw oil subsided, the situation has gradually become peaceful. However, harvests have not been very good in various places this winter, so the local supply is extremely scarce. Compared to previous years, new goods from Wenzhou, Taizhou, and Jiangxi would have already arrived in succession, but it is unexpected that all production areas report low supply and high prices, resulting in no arrivals from Taizhou and Wenzhou to date, and only nearly a hundred pieces of Jiangxi oil arriving. Therefore, the customer goods are almost extinct. Such a harvest situation is rarely seen. Merchants previously procured a batch from Yichang at a reasonable price, but the quality of the goods was slightly uneven. According to reports from the Wuhan market in recent days, the market remains firm, also due to weak arrivals. Although there are no large transactions in the sales market, sporadic sales are not weak. The initial quote for newly produced Zhongjing oil from the head plate the other day was 11 taels 8 qian of Caobao silver per piece. At this price, the cost to arrive in Shanghai would be around 20 yuan, but the current selling price of Zhongjing oil without wood in Shanghai is only 19.5-19.6 yuan, which is not in line with the cost. Therefore, the market outlook is very stable, but sales are not as good as in previous years because Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are both drought-stricken areas and candle sales are also unusually sluggish. It is truly said that the harvest determines the sales.

Woolen Overcoating Fabric Affected by the Weather

Woolen overcoating fabric is currently in its peak season, but sales are actually slower than in the autumn. Whether it is multicolored and iridescent fabric, double-sided or single-sided flocked, dotted, checkered, herringbone, or twill fabric, the trends are all loose and weak. The biggest reason is indeed the impact of the warm weather. According to this year's weather, it is sometimes sunny and sometimes rainy, unlike the deep cold winters of previous years, which has caused sales of this type of woolen overcoating fabric to slow down. Customers have reduced purchases of medium and Western-style thick woolen overcoats.

Free Talk

Emphasis and Exaggeration in Modern Art

— He Jin

Having spent ten years after the Great War groping and feeling suffocated by the loss of all methods, the people of the 1930s were indescribably happy when they suddenly saw the emergence of a new theory and new things. It was this power of revelry that blinded their comprehension and called them to pursue the light regardless. Thus, when the social system presented an unusually rapid transformation in a sudden manner, the stimulation they received was simply indescribable. All order, morality, and religion were shattered into pieces by a swift "no way" bomb. And the people living in these fragments also lost everything, leaving only naked primitivity.

At the same time, science and industry presented astonishing developments, and all things sufficient to produce new stimulation came into being: skyscrapers, airplanes, high-speed locomotives, speedboats...

In this contradictory conflict between economic depression and the rapid advancement of science and industry, some of the people of the 1930s inevitably had only one path to take: frenzy! They constantly pursued new stimuli to numb the current hardships. They only needed action, action, action—meaningless primitive action.

This formed what Americans called "Fast Life."

This tendency, expressed in modern art, is emphasis (Strong Tone) and exaggeration (Hypdrbole).

Due to the aforementioned reasons, what people in the 1930s yearned for was no longer meticulous fine-brush paintings, but the emphasized sketches and woodcuts of the Expressionists; no longer boating on the moon and lingering in low murmurs, but the speeding of speedboats in raging waves; no longer the seclusion of sounds, but the rapid playing of voices with extremely high frequencies. At the same time, due to the sweeping of "fast life," people no longer had time (or rather, did not have the mood) to appreciate medieval fine-brush paintings. They only demanded cartoons (Carton) in which certain characteristics were expressed particularly clearly with exaggerated techniques. They no longer wanted to savor the meticulous descriptive texts in newspapers; they could only read one or two summary headlines!

This technique, expressed in modern art, includes Picasso's paintings, E. Nolde's woodcuts, and common cartoons in painting; Richard Strauss's symphonies in music; and Ernest Hemingway and William Faulkner's novels, which worship primitive, naked action, and J. M. March's poems in literature.

If it is not denied that it is possible to interpret art with life, then the art of the 1930s perfectly represents the lives of modern people: emphasis, exaggeration! And this emphasis and exaggeration were only accepted in this crazy decade of the 1930s. Just look at the pre-war salons discarding Picasso, and pre-war people saying that Gertrude Stein's chapters could only be understood by herself and no one else. But look at the post-war 1930s: seeing people trying to imitate Picasso and Stein, one can understand.

Therefore, this emphasis and exaggeration are not only not "dazzlingly strange" as commonly said; on the contrary, they truly represent the "human suffering" of the 1930s.

A Certain Trip

— Ouyang Shan

I ran to Foshan Town with a large group of people of all kinds without a profession...

"Hanging out" with Cantonese people is a fun game with a strong flavor. It exceeds solidified comfort, vulgar enjoyment, and stale leisure, and is a tense adventure mixed with human sympathy. Everyone stares at their target with the agile and shrewd eyes of a hunter, making all kinds of beautiful and fanciful plans; at night, they gamble greedily until dawn. During the day, they spend all their money lavishly on food. A landlord's son from Yangjiang County, who was preparing to get a small job in the Minding Inspection Office, a character whose name seemed to be Gu Gengzhi, proposed a trip to me when he realized there was no hope at all.

"Wu Dakui, do you know what Yangjiang County is best known for? It's not leather suitcases and leather pillows, those are all fakes! It's the people who eat everywhere. That's really amazing!" He said this and patted his chest, as if he couldn't burp out a full stomach.

He opened his two old Chinese-style leather suitcases, picked up two or three newly pasted decoration boxes, which contained a dozen or more medicine bottles. He pointed to the boxes for me to see. Thousands or hundreds of small glass bottles, each two or three inches high, were filled with black oily fake medicine, scattered disorderly like two boxes of scattered large bullets: and he boasted to me:

"Prevention is better than cure, that's what this is! Don't look down on it, thinking it's just some fake medicine oil! Actually, where can you find real medicine?" He smiled affectionately at me and continued, "With it, I can go to any place I want, and most of the time there is not much difficulty. And, and..."

Distinguishing Characters and Distinguishing Words (I)

— Cao Juren

Guest: Ah, the level of Chinese of young people nowadays is really getting worse with each generation!

Host: Hmm, haven't seen you in a few days, you've turned into a "people's hearts are not as good as they used to be" type! "People's hearts are not as good as they used to be" is truly an ancient saying, there is such a sentence in the oldest Egyptian inscriptions ten thousand years ago. When you were carrying your schoolbag and studying at school, those old predecessors touching their beards were already saying: "The level of Chinese is really getting worse with each generation"; and now it's your turn to say it.

Guest: Brother, I'm not here to argue with you. I just flipped through those students' test papers on your desk, and some wrote "分岐" (fen qi, divergence) as "分岐" (fen qi), "生熟" (sheng shu, raw and cooked) as "生孰" (sheng shu), "蹤跡" (zong ji, trace) as "從跡" (cong ji), "著明" (zhu ming, notable) as "箸明" (zhu ming); some wrote "九仭" (jiu ren, nine ren, a unit of length) as "九軔" (jiu ren), "兩造" (liang zao, both parties) as "兩曹" (liang cao), "茫茫" (mang mang, vast) as "芒芒" (mang mang), "歌頌" (ge song, sing praises) as "歌訟" (ge song, singing accusations); such a series of wrongly written characters is something we have never seen before, isn't this the decline of young people's Chinese level?

Host: Haha, haha...

Guest: What are you laughing at? What are you laughing at? Am I wrong?

Host: I remembered a story that is quite similar to what you said, and I couldn't help but laugh. During the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty, there were two chief examiners, one surnamed Zhuang and one surnamed Ju. Zhuang was mediocre, and Ju was confused. Someone composed couplets using Du Fu's poems to mock them: "A dream unknown when will awaken, chrysanthemum flowers from now on need not bloom." After Ju finished the exam, he returned to Beijing and complained to Chen Jushan, the vice minister, "The Hangzhou personnel are not understanding, how can Ju connect to chrysanthemum?" Chen Taipu remained silent and did not answer. Ju asked him again, and Chen Taipu said, "I am thinking here about the phrase "chrysanthemum has yellow flowers" in the Book of Rites Monthly Orders!" Ju felt greatly ashamed. (See Miscellaneous Notes from the Two Kinds of Autumn Rain Hut). Now, please don't blush, let me explain them to you one by one. This sees the Explanation of Writing, look at the footnote under the character "岐" (qi, divergent): "Mount Qi, the mountain has two forks. Therefore, it is named." "岐" (qi) is the original character, and later a vulgar character "歧" (qi) was specially made to mean two forks. This here is the Book of Rites, look at the Ritual Evolution chapter: "Smelling the minced meat, cooking the millet." Explanation of Writing: "孰 (shu), cooking food." Commonly written as "熟 (shu)." Look again: "從跡 (cong ji)"'s "從 (cong)" is the original character, but "蹝 (xi)" is the vulgar character; "箸明 (zhu ming)"'s "箸 (zhu)" is the original character, but "著 (zhu)" is the vulgar character. Look again: "九仭 (jiu ren)," Mencius writes "digging a well nine ren"; "曹 (cao)," Explanation of Writing, the two prisons of a prison are also called cao. The Records of the Grand Historian writes it as "two encounters." 茫茫 (mang mang), in Fu: "芒 (mang). Mang Yu's footprints," Shang Ode:: "The flood is vast 芒芒 (mang mang)." all written as "芒芒 (mang mang)." Chu Ci: "Without care, he does not know where he steps (zhi)," Wang note: "Dan is taken also." "耽芒 (dan mang)," commonly written as "渺茫 (miao mang)." "訟 (song)" Explanation of Writing: "訟 (song), to contend, says 'sing accusation'. 頌 (song), appearance also. 容 (rong), containing also. Now "sing accusation" is written as "sing praise," and "praise appearance" is written as "appearance," all are vulgar errors. Brother, who is reading wrongly written characters? Who is writing wrongly written characters?

Guest: Oh! So I'm wrong?

Under his supervision and command, we abandoned our companions and set off without letting anyone know. Our destination was Gaoyao County, and our journey was more than 400 li of uneven mountain and water roads. He seemed very familiar with all the paths and went straight to Sanshui Division after passing Jinmaoding Mountain and Kuigang. I had diarrhea and took a ferry back alone, separating from him.

When walking, we were as slow as snails. Gu Gengzhi praised everything he saw, seemingly very fond of this kind of life. One night, we stayed in a small village's Doumu Temple. The shrine was very simple, without any light. He said to me cheerfully:

"Moreover, one person cannot take care of others well and also take care of themselves well. There must be something stuck there, everyone is equally stupid and can't come up with a solution. Don't you think so? So if you want to bite someone, don't just make a show of wanting to bite, that will definitely cause others to raise a wooden stick and beat you half to death. Bite down, and bite deep, right into the bone! The one you bite will know that they shouldn't yell out, and they have to pretend that nothing happened!"

Those women who liked to buy medicine proved these words to be true. One of them bought a bottle of medicine oil, opened it, and used her finger to apply a bit to her temple, immediately praising the peculiar efficacy of the medicine oil to the remaining women and the farmers who were watching idly.

"This is the good character of the Chinese people, my great disciple, let's go."

Gu Gengzhi said to me as he packed up the medicine box. So I picked up those luggage, sang Cantonese opera all the way, said thank you to everyone, and stepped into another village...

People sometimes have to live like this.

Loneliness

— Ma Xingye

Following over a month of continuous rain, the sky is so low, Nanjing has become a pot, and I am floating on the cold water in the pot. Lately, I've gradually felt an irredeemable sense of desolation. No friends come on Sundays. If I were to seek friends myself, Nanjing is an ice block to me. I cannot, nor am I willing to, be imprisoned on this ice block. I spent a Sunday with the doors tightly shut. At three in the afternoon, I turned on the electric light, the inside of the house as desolate as the outside. The electric light cast a pale glow on the newly tidied desk.

For the past half year, my emotions have been poor. What you earnestly hope for is intimacy, but when you encounter it, it immediately turns into noisy annoyance. You also earnestly hope for tranquility, but when there is tranquility, it immediately turns into desolate loneliness. Both noise and loneliness are very difficult to cope with. My nerves are gradually weakening. Rather than struggling and enduring in noise, it is better to lock myself in loneliness, to be frozen in desolation. I picked up Russell's (Conquest of Happiness), but my eyes kept wandering, unable to focus. So I pressed my index finger against my right cheek, closed my eyes, and pretended to sleep. Outside the window, it was still drizzling.

I remember this heart that has followed me for over twenty years, being enveloped in a sticky, ashen "loneliness," it has happened more than once. However, lately, I've become more aware of this sticky, ashen film. Last year, when the university had its summer vacation, and I was still attending summer school in a foreign land, when summer school ended and even the old ladies and gentlemen had left the university town, I also discovered my heart was locked in loneliness. However, you could go to the tennis court and toss a ball with the landlord's young children, you could sit in the rocking chair in front of the door, watching wisps of smoke rising from the chimney of the opposite house, you could wait for the newspaper boy to throw the rolled-up evening paper in front of your chair, and you could even take out a pencil to guess crossword puzzles. None of these things can be done now, and doing them would be too childish. I am too far from childhood.

Although the fire in the stove is not very big, I am unhappy with my stove for other reasons. This stove doesn't allow one to play with the fire properly. If it were an open fireplace, if it were burning wood blocks, I could use tongs to stir the red-hot wood blocks, causing golden sparks to continuously fly out. The fire could temporarily warm and redden one's face. Because I am playing with the fire, I wouldn't be afraid of getting too close and overheating. Descartes, in front of his stove, used his meditation and contemplation to understand the principle of the impermanence of creation. I absolutely do not want to use my brain like him. I just want the small sparks to relieve my loneliness.

If this stove were made of red clay, burning charcoal, it would be more interesting. The charcoal would crackle and pop, and sometimes suddenly explode, startling people, which could break this too-congealed silence. Moreover, I could boil some tea. A friend from Hangzhou recently sent me a can of good tea leaves. However, I would have to use tap water. You can never find any good spring water in Nanjing. I don't drink alcohol, so of course I can't boil wine to console my loneliness. Even if I were to boil tea, with such a dull and stupid stove, how could it brew good tea?

Gradually, it is dusk. Loneliness becomes even heavier. The newspaper vendor delivers the Shenbao, and a few muddy footprints are imprinted on the clean floor.

Smile (1)

— By Lawrence of England, translated by Tang Xiru

It was night again when he arrived at the "Blue Sisters" convent, chosen by Ophelia for her retirement. He was led into the prioress's room in this magnificent convent. She silently stood up, bowed to him, and lowered her eyes to look at him. Then she said in French:

"I am very sorry to tell you that she died this afternoon."

He was stunned, but did not feel much pain, only stared blankly into the void with his handsome, cold, monk-like face.

The prioress gently placed her soft white, beautiful hand on his arm, leaned close to him, and looked up at his face.

"Be brave!" she said softly. "Be brave, can't you?"

He stepped back a few paces. He was always terrified when a woman leaned so close to him. The prioress, even though she wore the voluminous habit, was still very feminine.

"I am very brave!" he replied in English. "May I see her?"

The prioress rang a bell, and a young nun ran out. Her face was very pale, but in her brown eyes, there was a kind of innocence and mischief. The old woman murmured an introduction, and the young woman gravely gave him a slight bow. But Matthew stretched out his hand, as if a man had reached his last shred of hope. The young nun slipped her soft white hand out of her sleeve, and shyly slid one hand into his, completely as docile as a sleeping little bird.

He crawled out from his melancholy, unfathomable shade. He thought, "What a beautiful hand!"

They walked along a beautiful but serene long corridor. Tapping on a door, Matthew walked as if in a fog, but still aware of the beautiful volume of the two women's black skirts, moving with soft, rustling haste in front of him.

When the door opened, he was stunned. He saw that in this high, magnificent room, many wax candles were burning around the white bed. A nun was sitting beside the candles. When she raised her head from her prayer book, her face under the white hood was somber and simple. Then she stood up, a robust woman. She bowed slightly to him. Matthew saw her dusky milky white hands, twisting a string of beads on her magnificent blue satin chest.

The three nuns gathered together silently. But as they went to the head of the bed, the pleats of their silk black skirts were still rustling, feminine. The prioress leaned down and, with the most graceful movement, lifted the white linen face covering from the dead body's face.

Matthew saw the dead and beautiful serenity on his wife's face. Suddenly, deep in his heart, a kind of emotion like laughter was stirring. His throat made a slight sound, and an extraordinary smile ran across his face.

The three nuns, in the flickering, rapidly and warmly trembling candlelight, like a Christmas tree, were constantly revealing a look of utmost sympathy beneath their hoods, looking kindly at him. They were like a mirror. Six eyes suddenly took on a kind of fearful surprise, then changed, bewildered, turning into a strange expression. On the faces of the three nuns, who had been looking helplessly at him in the candlelight, a strange, involuntary smile began to seep out. On these three faces, the same smile bloomed so differently, like three delicate flowers. On the pale face of the young nun, the smile was almost painful, with a mischievous, intoxicated meaning. But on the face of the nun watching over the dead body, the mature, dark-haired woman with straight eyebrows, there appeared a pagan smile, slow, with an infinitely cunning meaning in its decaying, humorous sense. This was an Etruscan smile: cunning, shameless, unanswerable.
