Shenbao Local Supplement

Talks

Zhao Xinbo Executed, Helpless

The damned Zhao Xinbo has now been executed by the Japanese. It is regrettable that Zhao Xinbo did not die under our national law, but at the hands of Japanese warlords. But to put it more bluntly, Zhao Xinbo did not die under our national law, but at the hands of Japanese warlords, and is especially damned.

According to a Tokyo-based newspaper's Shenyang dispatch, "The notorious traitor Zhao Xinbo was invited by Hishikari under the pretext of a banquet after returning from Japan to investigate constitutional government. After Zhao arrived, he was immediately executed." It is reported that there were four reasons for his death, and one of the four was that "Zhao mistakenly regarded the puppet organization as a genuine country. Therefore, when Manchus in the puppet organization were constantly deferring to the Japanese, he reprimanded them to their faces, causing the Manchus in the puppet organization to resent him." Zhao's death was due to this. The Japanese organized the puppet Manchukuo as a tool to deceive the world, a game of manipulating the Manchus. Therefore, all political power was in the hands of the Japanese. However, some traitors mistakenly believed that the Japanese had special goodwill towards the puppet Manchukuo. They celebrated and their faces were filled with joy, often taking it upon themselves to be loyal to the Qing dynasty and restore the Manchu Qing. They were truly dreaming a great dream.

There are quite a few traitors who are still dreaming this dream. It is said that the puppet Prime Minister Zheng Xiaoxu and his ilk also hold this view. Although they are now controlled by the Japanese, they also want to organize a genuine puppet Manchukuo country in the future. I think it would be best to dispel this idea. Zhao Xinbo is an example. It would be better to be obedient and quick to directly pledge allegiance to the Japanese, to become docile subjects of Japan, and not to sleep in the drum, dreaming of restoring the Manchu Qing.

After Zhao Xinbo was executed, the general members of the puppet organization who relied on Zhao for support were all crestfallen and extremely pitiful. In fact, these kinds of shrimp soldiers and crab generals are pitiful but not worth pitying. Zhao Xinbo was one of the giants among the traitors, and still couldn't see the wind, wanting to take it upon himself to organize a genuine puppet Manchukuo country, dreaming a spring dream. As for the general mob, they are even more unworthy of mention. But this is an opportunity for them to realize, so that they will not have this dream again in the future.

As for the cause of Zhao Xinbo's death announced by the Japanese, accusing Zhao of communicating with the interior is naturally absurd. As the saying goes, if you want to condemn someone, you can always find a pretext. Even if Zhao's current aim is to restore the Manchu Qing, he would never want to communicate with the interior. Even if he is not loyal to the Qing dynasty, as a traitor, his name is already very famous, and people in the interior would never want to associate with him. Therefore, Zhao's death is to kill the chicken to scare the monkeys. It is an example for traitors. I advise Zheng Xiaoxu and his ilk not to dream of restoring the Qing dynasty again.

After the Autumn Harvest

— Inside

As soon as it was light, the golden light of the sun gradually shone from behind the eastern mountains, illuminating this desolate hillside. The bleak autumn scenery was revealed here.

Gui Lang's pale, tired face looked particularly sallow in the morning sunlight. Since yesterday, he had run dozens of miles. His legs, heavily stepping on the hillside path, walked step by step towards the city.

For several years, the thousand steps of land rented by Gui Lang, the annual harvest, could be enough for his household expenses and rent, but this year, the sky was early, and the fields around Gongjia Town were all damaged by the sun. It hadn't rained for more than a month, and the large stream in front of the town was so dry that there was no water at all. Gui Lang's field, although close to the eastern neighbor of the large stream, was the same. The soil was cracked with streaks of marks, and the rice seedlings were withered and died. This declared despair for his autumn harvest this year, as desperate as the people of Gongjia Town.

The sky finally rained, but it brought the autumn climate.

Gui Lang, who was already pale and thin, is now even paler and more worried. In previous years, after this autumn harvest, in addition to paying the landlord's rent, he could barely get through this remaining winter. But this year, everything in front of him has changed.

Time is passing day by day, and the landlord has come to urge him three times in a row. Tomorrow, the fourth scheduled date is coming. This made Gui Lang feel even more depressed and urgent. Because of the approaching fourth rent period, Gui Lang has been running around trying to find a way for the past few days, but autumn harvest is hopeless for everyone in Gongjia Town, who else can help whom?

Several days of running around, all he got was despair, which made Gui Lang's heart even more anxious. He didn't sleep all night last night, and his head was a little dizzy, but tomorrow, the fourth scheduled date is coming. As soon as it was light, he walked out of Gongjia Town with a dizzy head and tired, weak legs, and stepped onto the path on the hillside leading to the city.

But when Gui Lang came back, he had an even more sad and decadent face, and slowly, he stepped onto the dead and silent path on the hillside again. At this time, he was filled with 120,000 points of fatigue, his footsteps showed even more weakness, but his heart, that anxious heart, was jumping violently.

The streets of the town, the shops were lit with kerosene lamps. Gui Lang entered the town at this time. He had run more than fifty miles of mountain roads since morning, but he hadn't eaten anything in his stomach. His legs were simply numb. At this time, he walked a few steps and stopped on the street, looking towards his home. Slowly, turning a few corners, he finally saw his dilapidated tile house, which was about to become someone else's property, and he sighed like a fool at the dark, leaden sky.

"How is it? You ran so tired, did you borrow anything?"

Gui Lang's wife, looking at Gui Lang's appearance, asked very anxiously and sadly. But Gui Lang, he. Shook his head with his eyes closed.

On the next day, the people who collected the rent for the fourth time came, but Gui Lang, walked into another world in the late night. Only his woman and son, were crying and scolding there.

Recalling Old Times in a Year of Famine

— Bing

丨丨Eating Row Meals丨丨

"Eating row meals," on the one hand, is an event like the Shanghai people say "it's fun to come and see," and on the other hand, it is the most tragic expression of people's misfortune.

I once witnessed this scene when I was very young. I can't remember the year, but I only remember that year there was also a drought. In the vast countryside, the drought was so bad that even drinking water became a problem. As for filling one's stomach with "eating," of course, there was no way to solve it. So the tragicomedy of eating row meals was played out.

The facts were strung together like this: Whether they are relatives or friends, they are usually familiar and get along well. But at this time, everyone couldn't care about anything. Everyone put down their usual faces and gathered together in a formation-like team, led by one or two leaders with more reliable leads. The order was very good, and they were very harmonious and friendly. When they arrived at a family's house, they dispersed and searched out all the things that could fill their stomachs from the whole family, cooked them, and everyone politely divided and ate them until there was not a single grain left. Then they went to the second family, and according to the original method, ate them one by one.

People's lives in the famine were only maintained in this way.

The name is "eating row meals," but in reality, there is not much rice to eat. As far as I remember, they usually drank porridge, because the famine was too severe. Ordinary wealthy families also became poor people. Everything they had was only enough for a large group of people to drink a few meals of porridge. Some could only find some miscellaneous grains, and they were also considered "eating row meals" in a sloppy way.

Here, there are several situations that are worth praising.

First, is the revelry of the children. They were originally ruled by the "naive gods," and didn't know what to call a "year of abundance," or what to call a "year of famine." As long as people and horses gathered together, they reveled and forgot themselves, regardless of whether this "gathering" was "tears" or "smiles"? At that time, I was also one of them. Watching the children of the east family and the children of the west family all gathered together to eat and drink, I didn't feel hungry, and only reveled, as if I had gone to "heaven."

Secondly, the general women, each of them put on a bitter face, and there was no such cheerful scene of chattering as usual. Some even had two lines of tears that were about to drip but not dripping on the corners of their eyes, and some were indeed crying secretly.

As for the men, they were after all great men. Although there was no laughter, there was also no crying. However, their faces were indeed different from usual. Their mouths were always longer, and their eyebrows were always. The most special sign was that they were very irritable, often scolding women, often beating children, and sometimes beating children until they cried and wouldn't stop, and even wanted the children to die. They also often gathered together in groups of three or five, talking about how to relieve the disaster, but that was all nonsense, and couldn't be put into practice.

Those who were usually rich people, also ate and drank with us at this time, which was even more hateful and pitiful. The food was so inferior, but to fill their stomachs and save their lives, they had to put down their "status," throw away their previous set of "stomachs," and slowly, no, quickly, swallow and choke. Otherwise, their noble lives, at this time, were only "valued" the same as ours.

However, this was the time between May and June when the old grain had run out and the new grain had not yet arrived. I still remember that after July, this scene was cleaned up, because although that was a year of famine, it was still less famine than now.

Recently, I received a letter from my hometown, saying that "eating row meals" has already started in the countryside. This may still be a very long period of time, alas, Amen!

Singing and Dancing

Homesickness

— Simon

Drifting alone on the lonely journey of life for a long time, that loneliness gradually changed from faint to strong, and all the things that have passed through these times are like footprints printed in many places, disappearing as they appear and disappear. Memory has not left a worthy impression to be forgotten forever from time to time. I feel that everything is a bit empty, and people are even more like stepping on a cloud of clouds, infinitely vague. I think to myself, this is probably because I have lived a few more years, and the childlike spirit has been eroded by the bustling world, making a person's thoughts very illusory, and lacking a keen interest in anything, especially a true taste. However, recently, it is strange that the thought of home, which I have not thought of for a long time and almost forgotten, has been brewing in my heart again. And some of the well-known scenery of my hometown can arouse my deep reverie. In the boundless reverie, there is also a kind of unspeakable intimate feeling, which makes me feel a heavy nostalgia for home.

I have been away from home for quite a while. During this time, I completely made myself a wanderer who really had no home, wandering everywhere. Home was thrown behind me as soon as I crossed the door. The people in the family are looking forward to my news every day, and after too long, letters of inquiry fly in constantly. Each letter is permeated with the kind thoughts of my kind mother and a heart of maternal love. But for this, there is often no emotional stirring, and the heart is like a stagnant pool of dead water. At most, it is just a faint smile, and it disappears without a trace. But now, because of the grinding of endless wind and frost, everything outside, in addition to giving various feelings of indifference and alienation of sadness, I have never obtained any spiritual gift in this long sea of people. Now I deeply feel that home has a very intimate taste, and home has stirred up heavy waves from the still dead water-like heart. The past was so indifferent to home that even I can't explain why now, and precisely because the past was so indifferent, it makes the present

Page 19

, but also mixed with some light-smoke-like hatred and unspeakable regret. This regret is really issued by inner guilt. It becomes a crime against family members, especially the kind mother. I regret it a bit, and I shouldn't have left home like that. For a long time, I didn't send back a message, so that my mother's worried heart was always worried, hoping every day, and finally passing away in the midst of disappointment every day. Maybe this long day will reduce the joy of this homeland and show more loneliness!

Thinking of the homeland across countless mountains, and the heart of a mother across countless seas, worrying about her son thousands of miles away, I almost froze, and a burst of sadness in my heart almost dropped tears. Eyes that have not been wetted by tears for a long time are now often wetted by the pull of home from time to time.

Everything at home is warmly engraved on memory.

When I was at home, I accidentally caught a small illness and lay in bed, my mother was busy all day long, taking care of the cold and heat, taking care of the medicine, almost ignoring other things, ran in and sat on the side of the bed, gently stroking my forehead with her hand, and asked gently: Do you feel better? She ran out and came back to ask again in a moment, do you want to eat something. Even if you don't take medicine, just such warm comfort can make the disease better. But at that time, I didn't feel that these rare human maternal truths were precious at all, but instead became temperamental because of my mother's endless nagging. If I get sick outside, what will happen? Isn't it just hiding quietly in the house alone, unable to hear footsteps or gentle voices. All I can hear is the sound of breathing alone in a groan. My mother's warm comfort? It is only warm review in my dreams. Now that I know that I should cherish it, my body is blocked in a different place with countless mountains and seas. Home, when can I go back to enjoy the joy of that paradise, let me throw myself into my mother's arms and quietly listen to the warm and gentle comforting voice, and restore my barren heart of the lost paradise!

Winter in Nanyang

— Er

At this time of year, when snowflakes are about to fall, Nanyang is at its hottest. Here in the north, we love to huddle around the stove, preferring to stay indoors to avoid the cold north wind. We cherish the faint sunlight and rush to bask in it. From morning till night, the wind is fierce and the cold heavy, causing people to shrink and shiver. But in the southern lands, those who live near the equator are constantly immersed in sultriness, dreading the scorching sunlight. They bathe in cold water all day long; before dawn, they must get up to douse themselves with cold water to wash away the heat. Wrapped only in a towel, they sweat profusely. During the day, the streets are dominated by the scorching sun, and like in the north, the cold wind drives away pedestrians.

Throughout the year, the sun relentlessly beats down, with little wind and even less rain. The farmland is often baked as hard as wasteland, making it difficult to believe that it will soon flourish like bamboo shoots after a rain!

Winter is a time of stagnation, filled with heat and barrenness. People are so listless, sitting under coconut trees or hiding indoors.

However, even in the perpetual heat, there are changes reminiscent of spring and autumn within a single day. When the sun sets, the sea breeze sweeps inland, bringing a cool evening breeze in the twilight, dispelling the heat completely. At this time, the streets fill with people, flowing like water against the waves, and the scene is alive with the vitality of spring. People are filled with energy and excitement.

They take off their towels, put on soft, thin short shirts and pants, slip on sandals, and step out of their doors, feeling the coolness on their faces. They stroll leisurely, enjoying the breeze, their hair and clothes fluttering in the wind. They feel completely refreshed, as if they have just emerged from a pool, and their spirits are particularly light. Watching the people drifting by, they feel a sense of detachment from the world, which can dispel the endless worries in their hearts. After being cooped up in the store all day, as evening approaches, they involuntarily feel their hearts floating on the evening breeze, gently swaying, making their limbs feel light and ready to fly. Ah, the evening breeze of Nanyang is truly full of rich poetic charm! After enduring more than half a year of stifling life in Nanyang, people mostly rely on this light, intoxicating evening breeze to pass the time. Those suffering from the cold in the icy winter of the north cannot help but yearn for Nanyang, separated by rivers and mountains, where a gentle and refreshing evening breeze is blowing! Moreover, the time in Nanyang is exactly the winter we are experiencing now.

As the night deepens, the cool breeze of Nanyang will become even more intoxicating. When dawn is about to break, the sea breeze gradually disappears, and the eastern heat seems to bring a sense of warm stagnation. However, after a cold shower in the early morning, the sky resembles the early autumn season, pale and somewhat desolate, with a gentle breeze still blowing, carrying a hint of autumn melancholy within its tenderness. Although not as lively, carefree, and intoxicating as the evening breeze, it still has its unique flavor, a light haziness filled with the vitality of spring. When the sun just rises above the horizon, it seems to radiate the full golden light of spring.

Some call Nanyang a land of perpetual spring, which is not an exaggeration. People living in this Nanyang, which feels like spring all year round, are filled with a sense of intoxicated warmth. The local people of Nanyang live such simple and leisurely lives under this intoxicating and gentle atmosphere. Most live in a few thatched huts, with only a few changes of light clothing. The women chew betel leaves with mouths full, displaying a certain romantic charm, resembling a life close to nature. Most people live for the moment, spending whatever they earn, lacking ambition. In this winter, Nanyang is just like spring, and the people of Nanyang live even more simply, leisurely, comfortably, and warmly! However, the people of Nanyang are also too complacent, somewhat like drunkards who love to drink all the time!!!

Storytelling with Stringed Instruments

Yao Xiao'an, Wang Ping, Pearl Tower

China and West (1040) 11:00 PM to 12:00 AM

Opening: "Standard Beauty"

Today's standard is the most fashionable. New terms are everywhere. He is like a crane standing among chickens, leading the way. He can be a model, a leader. Having that title of "standard" is truly glorious. I'll use it to describe a beauty in detail. Her eyes don't entice souls. Her figure is stout, not slender. Her skin and muscles are all dark. Her movements are naturally uncoquettish. Her voice is loud and clear, like a booming bell. She never appears in social gatherings. She discards all rouge and perfume. She doesn't bother to learn dancing. Her academic achievements in both Chinese and Western studies are not high. However, she is frugal, simple, diligent, and hardworking. Her physique is strong and enduring. Her attitude is dignified and sincere. She never says anything frivolous. Her clothes are all made in China, flag robes made of local cloth. She greets her parents every morning and evening, pleasing them. She is a filial daughter, rare in the world. She hates the modern men and women. She has no interest in romance, her ambition is lofty. Her family is wealthy, with ample money. She is arrogant and not at all proud. Seeing the suffering of bankrupt farmers in rural areas, she personally goes to the countryside to spend lavishly. Her heart is always filled with hatred for the Eastern barbarians. She is willing to serve on the frontier, going to the battlefield. Such women are rare today. They fully embody the four characters of "standard beauty." Please don't laugh at my outdated words. It's just that I'm sounding the alarm, not afraid of mockery. I speak earnestly and tirelessly.

They study different ways to apply rouge. They don't use face powder, but Western powder. Their faces are entirely red, like Jiang Boyue reincarnated. They wear a robe made of silk and gauze. The most important thing is that it fits well. Their jade arms are exposed, enough to make one's eyes burn. Their plump hips sway, enough to enchant. Bare feet are considered a modern style. They wear high-heeled leather shoes. They are enrolled in school. The important subject is love. The friends they make are all men. They wear Western suits and leather shoes, fashionable. Today, they go to the park in pairs. Tomorrow, they watch movies in pairs. They want to watch foreign movies. Because Chinese movies are not modern. They are deeply in love. They eat several courses of foreign food. They exchange photos. The so-called love work is completed. A matchmaker comes to arrange a marriage. They get married in a restaurant. From then on, they spend a happy honeymoon. Dear, kiss me. They are affectionate in March and April. They have resentment in May and June. They are jealous in July and August. They become enemies in September and October. In another two months, they will talk about divorce. It is truly like striking apart mandarin ducks. The husbands and wives each sweep the snow from their own doors. They marry quickly and divorce quickly. Afterwards, everyone talks about their love experiences.

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao, Film Special

A Brief History of Film Development (5)

— Wenying

(5) The Attitude Towards Star Worship and Publicity Power

Due to space limitations, I cannot describe all the steps in the development of the film industry in detail. Furthermore, since the rise of the "star system," I cannot record the deeds of every star or quasi-star. However, to understand the background of the film industry, we must briefly describe a significant and meaningful key point between 1912 and 1918, and tell you some interesting stories about the stars of that time.

Before we learn about the deeds of the stars of that time, we can first say that the audience's attitude towards the stars is different from now. When Francis X. Bushman was at his peak, the company believed that the fact that he was married and had children should not be announced. Bushman was a married man with five children, but his contract with the company clearly stated that these facts could not be announced under any circumstances. At that time, he worked at Essanay Corporation in Poem Valley, but his family could only reside in the countryside of Maryland. One day, he brought his family to Poem Valley. The company authorities found out and immediately called Bushman in, severely reprimanded him, and told him to immediately send his wife and children back to the countryside of Maryland to prevent the news of his marriage and children from being leaked.

Bushman was now in a dilemma. On the one hand, he could not violate the terms of the contract and the orders of the company authorities, and on the other hand, he could not summon and dismiss his wife at will. As a result, the news inevitably spread. Firstly, Bushman and his wife had a disagreement, and secondly, Bushman fell in love with Beverly Bayne, a female star colleague. As a result, Bushman and his wife had to agree to a divorce. Bushman and the company both knew that it was difficult to hide the news any longer, so they discussed and agreed to announce the news of Bushman's divorce from his wife and Bushman's marriage to Bayne at the same time. As expected, after these two news were announced, Bushman immediately lost his status as a star. Because a star who already had a wife and five children was not very romantic, who would still worship him?

The company, of course, did not want a big star that had been cultivated for many years to disappear overnight. Therefore, they sent an investigator to conduct a field investigation throughout the country. As a result, he returned from his investigations everywhere. He ran to Bushman's dressing room. He went in and held his head in both hands without saying a word. Bushman saw that the situation was not right and asked, "Is it really not going to work?" The investigator said, "Not only is it not going to work, you are simply finished." His star life really ended there. After a few years, he reappeared in the film "Ben-Hur," but his past glory had disappeared, and he could no longer hear the goddess of luck knocking on his door for the second time.

The above is just one example. If we open and review the old movie magazines from the past, we can find out how vague the audience's knowledge of the stars was at that time. At that time, movie stars were individuals with all kinds of admirable virtues. They were all born into noble families and admired Shakespeare. The publicists at that time were omnipotent. They could cover the eyes and ears of the world with one hand, preventing the truth from being leaked, and on the other hand, they could fabricate facts and deceive the fans. For example, Theda Bara's real name was Theodosia Goodman. She was clearly American, but the publicists said that she was born on the banks of the Nile in Africa. In fact, the real deeds of these stars were more beautiful, grand, vivid, and interesting than the publicists fabricated. But they had nothing to do after eating, and they had to create some news to deceive the audience. The audience now is not the same as before. They are used to real things and do not find it strange for a star to get married and have children.

Note: This article is not finished, because the original text is not complete, so I have to wait for the original text to continue.

Film Review

Review of "Righteous Guest's Strange Knife"

— Linghe

Menace — Cathay

The translation of the film title has now reached its peak! The four words "Righteous Guest's Strange Knife" sound stiff and don't seem like the title of a great film.

Furthermore, after being exposed to too many detective films, it is indeed difficult to arouse much interest. The same old structure and lack of principles create a murder story, and the so-called tension and stimulation obtained is the success of the detective film. Therefore, I have almost nothing to say about "Righteous Guest's Strange Knife."

However, I can tell the readers that the use of the sound effect of a rainstorm at the beginning of this film, implying that the subsequent plot will proceed in a tense atmosphere, is quite commendable.

After that, it is all the usual techniques used in every detective film, bringing in a few suspected murderers, hiding the real culprit with photography techniques, and finally revealing the truth. People are really familiar with this kind of thing.

In any case, it is enough to explain that this is a vulgar work.

"Elegy of Life" and "Emperor E and Empress Huang"

The relationship between folk songs and a nation is profound, which is a fact recognized by everyone. Therefore, the popularity of a folk song is the expression of a nation's national character. Sometimes, just a few dozen words of impassioned lyrics can excite the blood of an entire nation. At the same time, a few dozen words of stubborn and obscene lyrics can also weaken the spirit of the entire nation. Therefore, the impact of folk songs on society and the country can be said to be profound and significant. At the same time, film is a powerful tool for promoting national culture. Therefore, inserting one or two songs that fit the plot into the film not only forms an additional layer of power for the film itself, but also has a deeper impression on the development of the entire story in people's minds. The Yihua Company's blockbuster, "Elegy of Life," directed by Hu Rui, describes serious problems in current society, such as the painful situation of unemployed youth. The development of the story grasps the contrast between the rich and poor classes. Therefore, in order to strengthen the atmosphere of the play, two songs were specially inserted, namely "Elegy of Life," sung by Liming Hui, which represents the lament of the common people, and "Emperor E and Empress Huang," sung by Hu Ping, which represents the praise of the decadent life of a special class. Not only are the songs melodious and moving, but the lyrics are also heart-wrenching.

Ye Juanjuan is Trampled

Under the trampling hooves of ambitious people, a group of innocent northeastern people who have lost their homes flee to the interior. Yuan Meiyun and Ye Juanjuan are two beautiful flowers among these disaster victims. However, in extreme panic and a riotous crowd, Ye Juanjuan lost her lover, Wang Yin, and was tricked to Tianjin by Zhao Xue, a local thug, and offered to his master Yuan Mei as the supreme gift.

When the night lights are first lit, we can see the grand banquet at Yuan's mansion on the road. The lights are bright, and the high-ranking guests are seated. Laughter and shouting echo each other, which is very lively. But who knows that in a room of this grand and majestic Yuan Mansion, there is a pitiful girl like a lamb to be slaughtered, and Ye Juanjuan's pure virginity will be lost under Yuan Mei's trampling!

This is a scene in "Escape," directed by Yue Feng of Yihua Company. Because of the grandeur of the scenery and the large number of shots, it took more than a dozen hours to complete.

Film Anecdotes

— Luo Ping

Occasionally, in a small room, I talked with five or six friends about the famous films released in Shanghai in 1934. Someone suggested selecting ten of them. Therefore, from the twenty film titles that were temporarily thought of, ten were selected. Here, I might as well transcribe them: 1. Fugitive, 2. Long Live Freedom, 3. Puppet, 4. Mutual Aid, 5. Pen Battle Strong Power, 6. Art Sea Spring Light, 7. Count of Monte Cristo, 8. Merry Widow, 9. Boudoir Complaint, 10. Bo Ai Lane

Those who received three votes included 1. Merry Widow, 2. Returning to Truth, 3. I Love Her, 4. Little Great Man, 5. Orient Express, 6. Sad Red and Green, 7. Wealthy Family.

Lin Qin

(1)

Because the Soviets have "refugees," so Wuxi is filming "Wild Child," Nanjing is filming "Wandering Child," Suzhou, Children's Light: Because the United States has "A Fugitive," so... Chinese people have a little cleverness, that is, they know how to imitate.

(2)

Anyone who tends to get in front of the camera is called a "movie star," no wonder Chinese movie stars are so numerous and worthless.

(3)

When the screenwriter and the director disagree, a film will never be a complete success. But now, many actors simply write the script themselves, so there are fewer disputes.

(4)

Instead of trying to make the plot tense and powerful, desperately trying to find a way out in the subtitles is a clumsy display of a foolish director.

(5)

Someone said, "There are no non-romantic female stars." But the word "romantic" depends on how you interpret it.

Shen Bao Film Special Submission Guidelines

This publication is a film publication that assists in cultural publicity and art. Foreign manuscripts are very welcome. Once published, the remuneration will be generous.

Once the text is published, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

The text in this publication is mainly in vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

When submitting a manuscript, each article must be affixed with a seal, otherwise it will not be remunerated.

The space in this publication is limited, and the text should be as concise as possible. Each manuscript should be about 500 words.

If the submitted document is a translation, the original should be attached. English should be omitted where possible.

Unless otherwise stated in advance and postage for return is attached to the text, photos, etc., the publication will not be responsible for preservation or return.

Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper, do not write horizontally, and do not use a pencil.

If it is discovered that a manuscript has been submitted twice, or that the text has been copied, no remuneration will be given.

Film Novel

Police Detective's White Lies (7)

— Xin Zhi

Joan looked at Condon in disbelief, her hopes, she now understood, were dashed. She shrugged, put on her hat, and followed Condon to the police car. When John Mitchell heard that his daughter had been arrested on suspicion of shooting Azell, he roared and jumped up in anger. But the evidence was solid, and the landlady testified in court that they had rented the house together. Joan said she rented the house for Mary Mallory, but no one had seen Mary Mallory. No one had even heard of her. Dan Oliver had been missing for a long time. No one saw him go to that house. Moreover, Joan's fingerprints were clearly on the gun. Furthermore, when Condon arrived, Joan was the only one by the deceased's side. If Condon were to testify, based on all circumstances, the suspicion of Joan committing the murder would be further strengthened.

Mitchell ran to Condon, wanting to bribe him, to tell him not to testify in court. But Condon refused. He said, "No way. Even for Joan's sake, I can't do that." Mitchell angrily said, "Alright. I promoted you. If I could promote you, can't I ruin you?" Condon was surprised and said, "What? Promoted me? Are you saying my promotion to captain was due to your influence?" Mitchell said resentfully, "Of course. Didn't you know?" Condon said, "Oh, I see. You ruined Oliver and promoted me. Both methods are dishonorable." After he finished speaking, he angrily walked out. That night, he wrote a resignation letter and submitted it to the superintendent.

After Condon rejected Mitchell's request and submitted his own resignation, he was embarrassed to see Joan for many days. But finally, he couldn't bear it anymore. He went to the jail to see her. Their meeting this time was tense and painful. Condon stammered, "I didn't dare to come for several days because I thought you would hate me and refuse to see me." Joan said calmly, "What are you talking about? Taylor, how could I hate you? This is your duty, I understand very well." Condon paused, then suddenly said to Joan, "Joan, I thought of a way. If you could... marry me, they couldn't call me to testify in court." When Joan heard this, a look of joy immediately appeared in her eyes, but after a while, she slowly shook her head and said, "Since others cannot make you change your principles, I will not make you change your principles either." As she spoke, she placed her hands on Condon's shoulders and said, "Taylor, you know I would never lie to you. I did not kill Azell. I swear I didn't. You must believe me. Now our only way out is to find Mary Mallory or Oliver, and everything will come to light." Condon jumped up and said, "My dear, I'll go find them. Don't worry. I will definitely find them." As he spoke, he hugged Joan, kissed her sweet lips, and left. All the witnesses had been questioned, except for Taylor Condon, whose whereabouts were unknown. But at this time, Condon, like a hunting dog, was searching in all directions for Mary Mallory and Dan Oliver. Later, he actually found a clue. Not far from the city, in the mountains, he found a small wooden house where Mary Mallory and Dan Oliver were hiding. Almost effortlessly, Condon caught Oliver and brought him to the local jail. In the local jail, Oliver confessed that he had killed Azell Brantley. He also signed his confession. In this way, the real culprit had been caught, and Joan Mitchell was restored to freedom. On the night Joan Mitchell was acquitted in court, when Mitchell, Taylor Condon, and Joan walked down the steps of the hall hand in hand, a group of reporters, photographers, and newsreel reporters surrounded them. Mitchell muttered to himself, "This is the biggest news of the year." Taylor looked at Mitchell and smiled, "Chairman Mitchell, you are a powerful man in the local area. Can you get us a marriage license right away in this late hour!" (The End)
